ལས་འབྱུང་བས་དེ་འདྲའི་བསམ་ཚུལ་ཕྱིས་བྱུང་བ་ལས་དེ་སྔར་མ་བྱུང་བ་བཤད་པ་ནི་
རྣམ་པ་ཐམས་ཅད་དུ་མི་འཐད་དེ། སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་མ་བྱོན་པའི་སྔ་རོལ་དུ་དེ་
འདྲའི་བསམ་ཚུལ་བྱུང་བ་ནི་དེ་སྔའི་ཧིནྡཱའི་གཞུང་ལུགས་མང་པོ་ཡོད་པ་དང༌། ལྷག་
པར་དུ་བདག་ཅག་གི་སྟོན་པས་ཀྱང་གནས་བརྟན་པའི་གནས་འཇོག་གི་མདོ་དང་ཆོས་
ཀྱི་ཚིགས་སུ་བཅད་པ་དང་ཆེད་དུ་བརྗོད་པའི་ཚོམས་ལ་སོགས་པར་སྐྱེ་བོ་ཐམས་ཅད་
འགྲོ་བ་མི་ཡིན་པ་མཉམ་པ་དང་ཐམས་ཅད་ལ་རིགས་མཐོ་དམན་དང་ལས་སོ་སོ་ཡོད་
པ་སོགས་ཀྱི་རྣམ་གཞག་མ་གསུངས་བས་བདག་ཅག་གི་སྟོན་པའི་གསུངས་འདི་དག་
ཀྱང་ཕྱིས་སུ་བྱུང་བ་བཤད་དགོས་པ་ལས་དེ་ལྟར་ཅི་ནས་ཀྱང་མི་འཐད་དོ།།
རིགས་པ་གཞན་ཡང་སློབ་དཔོན་འདིའི་མཚན་ཐོག་རྙེད་བཞིན་པ་དཔེར་ན་ཤཱ་
རིའི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཟློས་གར་དང་། མཛེས་དགའ་བོའི་སྙན་ངག་སོགས་དང་། རྒྱ་
ནག་གི་བཙུན་པ་ཨིཏ་ཙིང་གིས་བཏུས་པའི་གསུང་དུ་མ་དྲངས་པ་དུ་མ་སྣང་ངོ་།།
དེ་ཡང་རྒྱ་ནག་གི་འགྱུར་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཞུ་བ་དེ་དེང་དུས་ཀྱི་མཁས་པ་ཚད་ལྡན་
ཕལ་མོ་ཆེས་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ལ་རྗེས་སུ་ཟློས་ཏེ་ཕྱིས་ཆོས་ཀྱི་གྲགས་པའི་
མཚན་ཅན་ཞིག་གིས་བརྩམས་པ་ཡིན་པ་གསལ་ཏེ། སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་གཞུང་གི་བརྗོད་བྱ་
དང་མི་མཐུན། གཞུང་དེའི་ནང་བརྗོད་བྱ་གཙོ་བོ་རིག་བྱེད་བཞི་བཀག་ལ། སློབ་དཔོན་
གྱི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཏུ་རིག་བྱེད་མི་བཀག་པར་རིགས་བཞི་བཀག་པ་མ་ཟད་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་
བྲམ་ཟེའི་གཞུང་ཚད་མ་རྣམས་དྲངས་ཏེ་འགལ་བ་ལྟག་འཕྲོད་དུ་བསྟན་པའི་ཕྱིར་རོ། །
དེས་ན་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཅེས་བྱ་བའི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཀྱི་བརྗོད་བྱ་ལ་བལྟོས་ཏེ་



48
སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ།
ཕྱིས་རྩོམ་མམ་ཕྱིས་ཀྱི་མཁས་པ་ཞིག་གི་སློབ་དཔོན་ལ་ཁ་འཕངས་པའི་གཞུང་ཞིག་
ཡིན་པ་གདོན་མི་ཟའོ།།
རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱིས་མཛད་པའི་སྒྲུབ་བྱེད་བསྟན་པ།
སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཅེས་བྱ་བའི་བསྟན་བཅོས་
འདི་སློབ་དཔོན་ཉིད་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པ་མ་ཟད་དེ་ཉིད་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་སྒྲུབ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཁུངས་དུ་
མ་བཤད་དུ་ཡོད་དེ། དང་པོར་གཞུང་དེ་ཉིད་ཀྱི་དབུའི་མཆོད་བརྗོད་དང་མཇུག་གི་མཚན་
བྱང་གི་སྐབས་སུ་སློབ་དཔོན་ཉིད་ཀྱི་མཚན་དངོས་སྨོས་པ་ལས་རྟོགས་ནུས་སོ།།
གཉིས་པར་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་མཁས་པ་རྣམས་ལ་སྔོན་ནས་ད་ལྟའི་བར་རླུང་ལྟར་
གྲགས་པས་ཐེ་ཚོམ་བྱ་བའི་གནས་སུ་འགྱུར་མི་དགོས།
གསུམ་པར་ཕྱི་རྒྱལ་གྱི་མཁས་པ་ཧཊསོན་གྱིས་དབྱིན་འགྱུར་མཛད་པས་དེ་
ཉིད་ཀྱིས་ཀྱང་སློབ་དཔོན་ཉིད་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པ་ལ་ཡིད་ཆེས་མཛད་ཡོད།
བཞི་པར་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་མཁས་པ་ཆེན་པོ་དང་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་ཞབས་ཞུ་པ་ལོཀ་མཱནྱ་
བཱལ་གདྨ་དྷར་ཏི་ལཀ་དང༌། ཨར་ཨེལ་མིཏྲ་རྣམས་ཀྱིས་སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་
མཛད་པ་བཞེད་དོ།།
ལྔ་པར་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་མཁས་པ་ཆེན་པོ་སྒྲ་གཅན་ནམ་རཱ་ཧུལསཾཀྲཏཡཱནས་སློབ་
དཔོན་ཉིད་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པར་ཡིད་ཆེས་མཛད་དོ།།



གླེང་བརྗོད། །
49
རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཀྱི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་མ་དཔེ་ཁག་
རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཅེས་བྱ་བའི་གཞུང་འདི་ལ་ཏ་ལའི་ལོ་མར་བྲིས་པའི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་
གྱི་མ་དཔེ་དང་དེའི་འདྲ་བཤུས་བྲིས་མ་ཁག་འགའ་ཤས་ཡོད་པ་རྣམས་ནི། །
༡ བངྒལ་ཨེ་ཤི་ཡའི་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་ཁང་དུ་བཞུགས་པའི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་གྱི་མ་དཔེ།
༢ པུནར་ཡོད་པའི་བྷནྡྲཀར་ཉམས་ཞིབ་མཐོ་སློབ་ཁང་དུ་བཞུགས་པའི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་གྱི་
མ་དཔེ།
གསར་
༢ མདྲ་པུརཱིར་ཡོད་པའི་ཨཊེཡར་དཔེ་མཛོད་ཁང་བཞུགས་པའི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་གྱི་མ་དཔེ།
༤ དབྱིན་ཡུལ་གྱི་ཀེམབྲེང་གཙུག་ལག་སློབ་ཁང་དུ་བཞུགས་པའི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་གྱི་མ་
དཔེ།
» ལོན་ཌོན་དུ་ཡོད་པའི་རྒྱ་གར་ལས་ཁུངས་ནང་བཞུགས་པའི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་གྱི་མ་དཔེ་

སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ།
རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་སྐད་རིགས་གང་དུ་འགྱུར་ཡོད་སྐོར།

རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཅེས་བྱ་བའི་གཞུང་འདི་སྐད་རིགས་དུ་མའི་ནང་འགྱུར་ཡོད་ཅིང་།
དེ་དག་གི་མཚན་བྱང་རིམ་པར་བཞིན་བཀོད་ན། །
༡ ཕྱི་ལོ་བརྒྱ་ཕྲག་བཅུ་པ་ e༧༣-2L༡ ལོར་དྷརྨ་དེཝས་ཏེ་ཆོས་ཀྱི་ལྷས་རྒྱ་ནག་གི་
སྐད་དུ་བསྒྱུར་ཅིང་དག་ཞུས་མཛད།
༢ ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡tre ལོར་འདི་ཉིད་ཛརྨན་གྱི་མཁས་པ་ཆེན་པོ་ཨེ། བེབར་གྱིས་ཇརྨནིའི་
སྐད་དུ་འགྱུར་ཏེ།ཨེ་བི་ཨེ་མིང་ཅན་གྱི་རྩོམ་ཤོག་ནང་དུའང་ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡tre ལོར་
བཀོད་ཡོད།
༣ ཉི་ཧོང་ངམ་ཇཔན་གྱི་མཁས་པ་ཏ་ཀ་སུ་ཀུས་ཉི་ཧོང་གྱི་སྐད་དུ་བསྒྱུར། །
༤ ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡༢༠ དང༌ ༡༤༣ ལོར་ཐོག་མར་དབྱིན་ཇིའི་སྐད་དུ་བི་ཨེཅ་ཧོཌསོན་དང་
ཨེལ་ཝིལཀིནསོན་གྱིས་བསྒྱུར་ནས་དཔར་དུ་བསྐྲུན། །

འགྱུར་གནང་ནས་ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡༩༤༩ ལོར་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་གཙུག་ལག་ཁང་ཆེན་པོ་
ཤཱཏིནིཀེཏན་ནས་དཔར་སྐྲུན་གནང་།།
s ཕྱིས་རྒྱ་གར་མཁས་པ་ཆེན་པོ་ལལནཇིགོཔཱལ་གྱིས་ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡༩ev ལོར་འབྱིན་སྐད་
དུ་ཕབ་འགྱུར་གནང་།
༧ ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡ear ལོར་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་མཁས་པ་ཆེན་པོ་ཌོགཊོར་རཱམཱཡཎཔྲསཱད་དཱིབེདིས་
ཧིན་སྐད་དུ་ཐོག་མར་བསྒྱུར་བ་མ་ཟད། ཕྱི་རོལ་པའི་ལུང་ཚིག་གི་མཚམས་སུ་ཕྱི་
རོལ་པའི་བསྟན་བཅོས་གང་དང་གང་ནས་དྲངས་པའི་ཕྱག་དཔེ་དེ་དག་གི་མཚན་
དང་ཤོག་གྲངས་ཁ་སྐོང་ལྷན་ཐབས་རྣམས་སུ་དེའི་ནང་གསལ་བའི་སྔོན་ཕྱི་རོལ་
པའི་དྲང་སྲོང་གྲགས་ཆེ་བ་རྣམས་ཀྱི་ལོ་རྒྱུས་རྣམས་གོ་བདེ་ཞིང་གཟིགས་བདེ་བའི་
སླད་རྣམ་ཐར་མདོར་བསྡུས་པ་རེ་ཡང་བཀོད་པ་སྣང་། གཞུང་འདི་ཉིད་རྒྱ་གར་ཝཱ་རཱ་
ཎ་སཱིའི་ཧིནྡྲའི་གཙུག་ལག་སློབ་ཁང་ཆེན་པོ་ནས་ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡༩Lv ལོར་དཔར་སྐྲུན་
མ ཛོད། འདིའི་ནང་གི་ལུང་ཁུངས་ཤས་ཆེ་བ་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་མཁས་དབང་
སུཛིཏཀུམཱརམུཁོཔདྡྷཡའི་སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ་ཅེས་
པའི་གཞུང་ཉིད་ལ་གཞི་བཅོལ་ཏེ་མཆན་དུ་ཕབ་པ་ལྟ་བུ་སྣང་།
ཕྱིས་འདི་ལྟ་བུ་གཞུང་གལ་གནད་ཆེ་ཞིང་ཕན་ཐོགས་ཆེ་བས་རང་རེ་བོད་སྐད་
དུ་དུས་ད་ལྟའི་བར་དུའང་མ་འགྱུར་བར་བརྟེན་རང་རེ་བོད་ཀྱི་རིག་གཞུང་ཡར་རྒྱས་
གོང་འཕེལ་གཏོང་འཆར་གྱི་གྲལ་ནས་ཡ་བྲལ་དུ་འགྱུར་རོ་སྙམ་པ་དང་། རྒྱ་གར་དུ་ཕྱི་

རོལ་པའི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཁག་ཏུ་འདིའི་ནང་གི་བསྟན་དོན་དང་ལོ་རྒྱུས་རྣམས་རྟོགས་སླ་
བའི་ཆེད་ངལ་བ་དང་དུ་བླངས་ནས་འདས་པའི་ལོ་ཤས་ནང་འདི་ཉིད་བོད་སྐད་དུ་ཕབ་
བསྒྱུར་ཞུས་པ་མ་ཟད་དབྱིན་ཧིན་གཉིས་སུའང་ཕབ་བསྒྱུར་དང་སྦྲགས་ལེགས་སྦྱར་མ་

ལ། མཚན་ཁ་ཅིག་ཏུ་ཐེག་པ་ཆེན་པོ་ལ་དད་པ་བསྐྱེད་པའི་བསྟན་བཅོས་བསྡུས་པ་ཞེས་

གནས་སྟངས་དང་། རིག་གཞུང་། ལེགས་བྱང་། ཆོས་ལུགས་འདྲ་མིན་རྣམས་གང་དང་
གང་ལ་མོས་གུས་ཡོད་ཚུལ་དང༌། མུ་སྟེགས་པ་རྣམས་ཕྱི་རོལ་པའི་ལྷ་དགའ་བྱེད་རཱམ་
ཡན་རྟོགས་བརྗོད་ཆེན་མོ་དང་། རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་སྐྱ་སེངས་ཀྱི་བུ་ལྔས་གཡུལ་དགྱེས་ཀྱི་
གཏམ་རྒྱུད་ཆེན་མོ་སྟེ་མཱཧ་བྷཱརཏ་བཅས་ལ་རྩེ་གཅིག་གི་སྒོ་ནས་དད་པ་ཡོད་པས་དེ་ཉིད་

གླེང་བརྗོད།
།
གྲགས་ཆེན་པོ་ཡོད་རྐྱེན་གཞུང་དེ་ཉིད་ལས་ཀྱང་ལུང་འདྲེན་མི་ཉུང་བ་ཞིག་བཞེས་
གནང་མཛད་ཡོད།
གཞུང་དེ་ཉིད་ནང་ལྟ་གྲུབ་ཀྱི་སྒོ་ནས་ཕྱི་རོལ་མུ་སྟེགས་པའི་བསྟན་པ་དང་།
གཅེར་བུ་པའི་གྲུབ་མཐའི་ལྟ་བའི་རྣམ་གཞག་ལ་དགག་བཞག་དང༌། ཁྱད་པར་དུ་རིག་
པ་ཅན་པ་དང་གྲངས་ཅན་པའི་གྲུབ་མཐའ་སྨྲ་བ་རྣམས་ཀྱི་ལྟ་བ་ལའང་སྐྱོན་བརྗོད་དུ་མ་
མཛད་པ་སྣང་ངོ༌། །དེས་ན་གཞུང་དེ་ཉིད་ཧ་ཅང་གལ་གནད་ཆེ་ཞིང་བོད་སྐད་དུ་ད་
ལྟའང་མ་འགྱུར་པ་ནི་ཧ་ཅང་བློ་ཕམ་ཆེ་བ་སྣང་། རིང་པོ་མ་ཐོགས་པར་དེ་ཉིད་བོད་སྐད་
དུའང་འགྱུར་དགོས་པས་བསྟན་པ་ལ་ཞབས་འདེགས་མི་དམན་པ་ཞུ་འདོད་པ་རྣམས་
ཀྱིས་འདི་ལྟ་བུའི་གཞུང་ངེས་པར་འགྱུར་གལ་ཆེ་བའོ་ཞེས་ཞུ་རེས་ཐལ། གཞུང་འདི་
ཉིད་ཀྱི་ལེགས་སྦྱར་མ་དཔེ་རྩ་བརླག་ཏུ་སོང་ཟིན་པས་ལེགས་སྦྱར་མ་དཔེ་ད་ལྟ་མ་
བཞུགས་ནའང་། རྒྱ་ནག་གི་སྐད་དུ་ད་ལྟའང་མ་ཉམས་པ་གནས་ཡོད་ཅིང་། དེ་ཉིད་ཕྱི་
གླིང་པ་ཕྲེསྒྲ་སྐད་དུ་གོང་མོས་བཞིན་ཕྱི་ལོ་ ༡༩༠༤ ལོར་འགྱུར་ཟིན་པ་གསལ།
སྙན་ངག་གི་གཞུང་།
མཛེས་དགའ་བོའི་རྟོགས་བརྗོད།
མཛེས་དགའ་བོའི་སྙན་ངག་གི་རྟོགས་བརྗོད་ཀྱི་གཞུང་འདི་དེ་སྔ་བོད་སྐད་དུ་
མ་བསྒྱུར་བར་ལུས་ཤིང་། ཉེ་ཆར་ལ་དྭགས་ཀྱི་མཁས་དབང་བློ་བཟང་འཇམ་དཔལ་
ལགས་ཀྱིས་དཀའ་ཚེགས་དུ་མས་འཁུར་དུ་བཞེས་ནས་ལེགས་སྦྱར་མ་དཔེ་ལ་གཞི་

སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ།།
བཅོལ་ཏེ་བོད་སྐད་དུ་ཆ་ཚང་བ་བསྒྱུར་ཏེ་བོད་འགྱུར་རྒྱ་གཞུང་གསར་པ་ཞིག་གོ །
གཞུང་གི་ནང་ལེ་ཚན་ ༡༤ ཡོད་ཅིང་། སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་སྙན་ངག་
གི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཆེན་པོ་གཉིས་པ་ལྟ་བུ་ཡིན་ཞེས། རྒྱ་གར་འཕགས་པའི་ཡུལ་ན་རླུང་
ལྟར་གྲགས་ལ། མཁས་པ་ཁ་ཅིག་གིས་འདི་ཉིད་སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་སྤྱོད་པ་ཞེས་བྱ་བའི་སྙན་
ངག་ཆེན་པོའི་ཁ་སྐོང་གི་ཚུལ་དུ་མཛོད་ཅེས་བཤད། གང་ལ་ཞེ་ན། སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་སྤྱོད་
པར་སྟོན་པའི་མཛད་རྣམ་མདོར་བསྡུས་ཏེ་བརྗོད་པ་རྣམས་འདིར་རྒྱས་པར་སྤྲོས་སོ། །
གཞུང་གི་རང་བཞིན་ནི་ཚིགས་བཅད་དུ་བཞུགས་ཡོད་ཀྱང་རྩོམ་ཧ་ཅང་བཟང་ཞིང་ཚིག་
སྦྱོར་ལེགས་ལ་ཚིག་དོན་གོ་སླ་བས་སྐྱེ་བོ་ཕལ་མོ་ཆེ་རྟོགས་པར་དཀའ་ཚེགས་མེད་ཅིང་།
གནའ་སྔ་མོར་གཞུང་དེ་ཉིད་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་གྲོང་དང་གྲོང་གསེབ་ཁག་ཏུ་གླུ་ལེན་མཁས་པ་
དང་བཞད་བགད་པ་མཁས་པ་རྣམས་ཀྱིས་དབྱངས་ཀྱི་ཚུལ་དུ་འདོན་ཞིང་སྒྲོགས་ཏེ་ཡུལ་
མི་རྣམས་བདག་ཅག་གི་སྟོན་པ་ལ་ལྷག་པར་དད་གུས་སྤྲོད་པར་བྱེད་པ་སེམས་སོ།།
བལྟ་བྱའི་སྙན་ངག་གི་གཞུང་ཚན།
སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་ཤེས་རབ་ཀྱི་རྣམ་དཔྱོད་རྩལ་དང་ལྡན་པ་རྣམས་ལ་
གོ་བདེ་བ་སྙན་ངག་གི་ལམ་ནས་སྟོན་པའི་བདག་ཅག་གི་སྟོན་པའི་མཛད་པ་རྣམ་ཐར་
དེའི་སྐབས་ཀྱི་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་དང་བསྟུན་ཏེ་རྣམ་ཐར་དང་སྦྱར་བ་སྐྱེས་རབས་སོ་བཞི་དང་།
མདོ་ཡི་རྒྱན་གྱི་གཞུང་ལྟ་བུ་བཅད་ལྷུག་སྤེལ་མར་མཛད་པ་དང༌། ཚིགས་བཅད་རྐྱང་
པའི་ངོར་སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་སྤྱོད་པ་དང་མཛེས་དགའ་བོའི་སྙན་ངག་གི་གཞུང་གཉིས་
མཛད་པ་ཡིན་ལ། དེའི་སྐབས་ཀྱི་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་ནང་ཤེས་ཡོན་ཅན་ཉུང་ཤས་ལས་མ་མཆིས་

པས་ཡུལ་མིའི་སྤྱིའི་ཆེད་སྟོན་པ་དང་དེའི་རྗེས་སུ་འཛིན་པའི་སློབ་མ་རྣམས་ཀྱི་རྣམ་ཐར་
བལྟ་བྱའི་སྙན་ངག་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་ལམ་ནས་བརྩམས་པ་འགའ་ཞིག་ཡོད་ཀྱང༌། སྔོན་བྱོན་
གྱི་ལོ་ཙཱ་བ་རྣམས་ཀྱིས་དེའི་སྐབས་བོད་མི་རྣམས་ལ་དེ་ཙམ་གྱི་ཉེ་བར་མི་མཁོ་བ་
དགོངས་ཏེ་རེ་ཞིག་བོད་སྐད་དུ་མ་འགྱུར་བར་ལུས་པའམ་དཔེ་ལག་སོན་མ་བྱུང་བའི་
རྐྱེན་གྱིས་ད་བར་ལུས་པ་ཅི་ཡིན་ཆ་མ་རྟོགས། ཕྱིས་སུ་རྒྱ་གར་ནང་དུའང་ཀླ་ཀློའི་དཔུང་
འཇུག་དང་མུ་སྟེགས་པའི་ངན་བྱུས་ཕྱི་གླིང་པའི་ཕྲག་དོག་སོགས་ཀྱིས་སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་
བསྟན་པ་མཐའ་དག་ཡང་དག་པ་འཛིན་པ་དང་བཤུལ་འཛིན་ཕར་བཞག གནས་ས་ངོས་
འཛིན་ཡང་མ་ཐོབ་པར་ཤིན་ཏུ་ཉམས་དམས་སུ་གྱུར། ལྷག་པར་དུ་རྩ་ཆེའི་གསུང་རབ་
དུ་མ་ནི་གཏོར་བསྲེག་གིས་རྐྱེན་པས་རྩ་མེད་དུ་སོང་ཞིང་། ད་ལྟའི་ཆར་ཅུང་ཟད་མིག་
ལམ་དུ་ཡོད་པ་ཁག་ནི་འཕགས་ཡུལ་ནས་ཡུལ་གྲུ་གཞན་དང་གཞན་དུ་དེའི་སྐབས་ཀྱི་
སངས་རྒྱས་བྱང་སེམས་ཀྱི་སྤྲུལ་པའི་ལོ་ཙཱ་བ་དང་པཎྜི་ཏ་རྣམས་ཀྱིས་རང་གི་སྲོག་བེན་
དུ་བཙུགས་ནས་ཡུལ་ཁམས་གཞན་དུ་ཐོས་བསམ་གྱི་ས་བོན་བཏབ་པ་ལ་བརྟེན་ནས་ད་
ལྟ་སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་བསྟན་པའི་དབུགས་ཀྱི་རྒྱུ་བ་མ་འགགས་པར་ཕྲན་བུ་རྒྱུ་ཞིང་གནས་
པ་མ་ཟད་སྔོན་གྱི་གནས་ཆེན་ཁག་ཀྱང་ཉིན་རེ་བཞིན་ངོས་འཛིན་གསར་པ་ཐོབ་ཏེ་མིག་
ལམ་དུ་འགྱུར་ཐུབ་ཙམ་ཡོད་དོ།། ་
བལྟ་བྱའི་སྙན་ངག་གི་ཁོངས་སུ་གཞུང་གྲགས་ཆེ་བ་ལྔ་ཡོད་པ་རྣམས་ནི།།
༡ ཡུལ་འཁོར་སྐྱོང་གི་ཟློས་གར།
༢ དབང་ལྡན་མ་དང་བྲལ་བའི་ཟློས་གར།
༣ གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་དང་པོ། ཤཱ་རིའི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཟློས་གར།



སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ།
༤ གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་གཉིས་པ། ཤཱ་རིའི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཟློས་གར།
» གཟུགས་ཅན་མ་ལྷག་མ་གསུམ་པ། ཤཱ་རིའི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ཀྱི་ཟློས་གར།
དང་པོ། ཡུལ་འཁོར་སྐྱོང་གི་ཟློས་གར།
སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་གཞུང་འདི་རིག་གནས་ཆུང་བ་ལྔའི་
ནང་ཚན་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཀྱི་གཞུང་ཆུང་ཞིག་ཡིན་ལ། ད་ལྟ་གཞུང་འདིའི་
མཚན་ཙམ་ལས་སྐད་རིགས་གཞན་གང་དུའང་མཇལ་རྒྱུ་མེད། དེ་ཡང་མཁས་དབང་
རཱཧུལ་སཾཀྲྀཏྟཡན་དང་ནུབ་ཕྱོགས་ཀྱི་མཁས་པ་སིལ་ཝིན་ལེ་ཝི་གཉིས་ནས་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་
བསྟན་བཅོས་འདི་འདྲ་ཞིག་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱིས་མཛད་ཡོད་པ་བཤད་ཅིང་། འོན་ཀྱང་རྒྱ་གར་
གྱི་མཁས་དབང་སྟོབས་ཀྱི་ལྷས་ལེགས་སྦྱར་གྱི་རྩོམ་རིག་གི་བྱུང་བ་”ཞེས་པའི་གཞུང་
ནང་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཞབས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་འདི་ཉིད་རྒྱལ་བ་པའི་
མཁས་པ་ཝཱདིརཱཇསཱརཱིས་མཛད་པའི་རིགས་པ་རྣམ་པར་ངེས་པའི་རྣམ་བཤད་ཅེས་པའི་
གཞུང་ནང་བཀོད་ཡོད་པ་མ་ཟད། ཡུལ་འཁོར་སྐྱོང་གི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་མདོ་འཛིན་པའི་ངག་
བཅས་ཀྱང་བཀོད་ཡོད།
མཁས་པ་འགས་འཕགས་པ་གནས་བརྟན་སྡེ་པའི་ལུང་བར་མའི་མདོའི་ནང་
ཡུལ་འཁོར་སྐྱོང་བའི་མདོ་ལ་ཁུངས་བཅོལ་ཏེ་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་འདི་ཉིད་
See, A History of Sanskrit Literature, p. 173, published by Sāradā Niketan,
varanasi, 1999. The portion of the text reads thus-f: ཝུབཤ :? ཀཱ
राष्ट्रपालं नाटकम्। कीदृशं च तन्नाटकम्? इति प्रसङ्गमारचय्य 'नाद्यन्ते ततः प्रविशति सूत्रधारः'
इत्यारभ्य पठति, नृत्यति, गायति च, अपरस्य व्यामोहनमनुवादे शक्तिव्याघातं च कर्तुमिति,
तदपि वादिनां निग्रहम-प्रस्तुताभिधानात् ॥ (न्यायविनिश्चयविवरण, भाग २, पृ० २३९)



གླེང་བརྗོད། ་་་་་་་
བརྩམས་པར་བཞེད། དེའི་རྒྱུ་མཚན་ཡང་དེའི་ནང་གི་འདྲེན་པའི་མཚན་ཡང་ཡུལ་འཁོར་
སྐྱོང་ཡིན་པར་བཤད། དེ་ཡང་ཁྱིའུ་ཡུལ་འཁོར་སྐྱོང་ཕ་མ་གཉིས་ཀྱི་བུ་གཅིག་པ་དང་
སྡུག་པ་ཡིན་པས་ཕ་མས་ཐོག་མར་བུ་རབ་ཏུ་བྱུང་བར་མ་གནང་། འོན་ཀྱང་སྨྱུང་བཅད་
པ་སོགས་ཐབས་མང་པོས་རྒྱུ་བྱས་ཏེ་མཐར་རབ་ཏུ་བྱུང་ཡང་ཕ་མ་གཉིས་ཀྱི་སར་ལོ་
རེར་ཡོང་བའི་དམ་བཅས་པའི་རྗེས་ཐོགས་སུ་སངས་རྒྱས་ཀྱི་བསྟན་པར་རབ་ཏུ་བྱུང་
ཞིང་། རབ་ཏུ་བྱུང་ནས་ཀྱང་བློ་གྲོས་ཀྱི་འཇུག་པ་མྱུར་བ་དང་གུས་རྟག་གིས་བརྩོན་
འགྲུས་བསྟེན་པས་རིང་པོར་མི་ཐོགས་པར་དགྲ་བཅོམ་པའི་གོ་འཕང་མངོན་དུ་བྱས། དེ་
ནས་ཉིན་ཞིག་སྟོན་པ་ལས་གནང་བ་ཞུས་ཏེ་རང་ཁྱིམ་དུ་ཕ་མ་དག་མཇལ་ཡང་ངོ་མ་
ཤེས། བསོད་སྙོམས་ངན་ངོན་གྱིས་ཚིམ་པར་མཛད། སླད་ཀྱང་རང་ཁྱིམ་དུ་བྱོན་པས་ཕ་མ་
དང་སྔར་རང་གི་ཆུང་མས་ངོ་ཤེས། ཁྱིམ་དུ་བཞུགས་པར་བསྐུལ་ཀྱང་ཁྱིམ་ནས་ཁྱིམ་མེད་
པར་རབ་ཏུ་བྱུང་བས་དེ་ཁོ་ན་ཉིད་ཀྱི་ཟབ་མོའི་ཆོས་ཤེས་སོ། ཡོངས་སུ་ཤེས་སོ་ཞེས་
བརྗོད་ནས་རང་གི་ཁྱིམ་ནས་དོང་ངོ༌། །ཆུང་མས་སླར་འབྱོན་པར་བརྣག་སྟེ་འགུག་ཀྱང་
སླར་ཁྱིམ་དུ་མ་བྱོན་པའི་ལོ་རྒྱུས་དང་སྦྱར་བའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཞིག་ཡིན་པར་

གཉིས་པ། དབང་ལྡན་མ་དང་བྲལ་བའི་ཟློས་གར།
གཞུང་འདི་ཉིད་ནི་ད་ལྟ་ཐོབ་བཞིན་པའི་སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་
པའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་དང་པོ་ལྟ་བུ་ཡིན་ལ་འདིའི་འདྲེན་མ་དབང་ལྡན་མ་ཡིན་

སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ།
SET
ཅིང་། དེ་ཡང་རྒྱ་གར་གྱི་མཁས་དབང་རཱཧུལསཾཀྲྀཏུཡནས་བརྩམས་པའི་ཝོལྷ་ནས་གདྨ་
བར”ཞེས་པའི་ཕྱག་དེབ་ནང་དུ་སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་སྔོན་མུ་སྟེགས་པ་ཡིན་པའི་སྐབས་
ཤིག་ན་ཡུལ་གནས་བཅས་སུ་ཡཱཝནའི་རིགས་ལས་མཆེད་པའི་བུད་མེད་མཛངས་མ་
འོད་ཟེར་མ་ཞེས་བྱ་བ་ཞིག་དང་ཕན་ཚུན་དགའ་ཞིང་བརྩེ་བ་ཆེས་ཆེར་རྒྱས་པ་བྱུང་བ་
ཡོད་ཀྱང་རིགས་དང་གོམས་སྲོལ་ཐ་དད་པའི་དབང་གིས་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་ཀྱི་གནས་སྟངས་
མཁྲེགས་བཟུང་གིས་རྐྱེན་པས་ཁྱིམ་ཐབ་མ་བྱུང་བའི་རང་རྣམ་དང་སྦྱར་བའི་སྒོ་ནས་
ཟློས་གར་ཞིག་མཛད་པར་བཞེད་ནས་ཕྱིས་སློབ་དཔོན་གྱིས་དབང་ལྡན་མ་དང་བྲལ་བའི་
ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཞེས་པ་འདི་ཉིད་ཟུར་དུ་མཛད་པ་ཡིན་ཅེས་བཤད། དེ་ཡང་
ཟློས་གར་དེ་ཉིད་འཁྲབ་སྟོན་ཐེངས་དང་པོ་གནས་བཅས་སུ་འཁྲབ་པ་མ་ཟད། ལེགས་
སྦྱར་ཐོག་འཁྲབ་པ་ཡང་དང་པོ་ཡིན་པ་རཱཧུལས་བཤད། དེ་ནས་ཡུལ་དང་ཡུལ་གྲུ་ཀུན་ཏུ་
དར་ཁྱབ་ཆེན་པོ་བྱུང་ཡང་ད་ལྟ་ལེགས་སྦྱར་ཐོག་གཞུང་འདི་རྙེད་སོན་མེད། །
ཡང་མཁས་པ་ཁ་ཅིག་གིས་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་ཁྲབ་གཞུང་འདིས་མཛངས་མའི་
བཞིན་མདངས་དང་སྒེག་ཉམས་རྣམས་ཡིད་ལ་རྟག་ཏུ་འཁོར་བཞིན་ཡོད་པས་དེ་ཉིད་
དང་བྲལ་བའི་སེམས་ཁྲལ་སྐོར་གྱི་རྣམ་འགྱུར་བསྟན་པའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་

གསུམ་པ། གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་དང་པོ།?
གཙ
ཤཱ་རིའི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད། སྲོཕེསར་ལུཊརྨ་ཞུ་བས་ཨེ་ཤེཡ་དབུས་སུ་ཏུནྟུན་ཞེས་
པའི་ས་གནས་ཧ་ཅང་རྙིང་པ་ཞིག་ཏུ་ཏ་ལའི་ལོ་མར་བྲིས་པ་གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་
གསུམ་གྱི་མ་དཔེ་ཆ་མ་ཚང་བ་ཞིག་ཐོབ་ཅིང་། དེའི་ནང་ནས་གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་
དང་པོ་དེ་མཆོག་ཟུང་ཡ་གྱལ་ཤཱ་རིའི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ཡིན་པ་ངེས་རྙེད་བྱུང་ཞིང་། དེ་ཉིད་
གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་དང་པོ་ཡིན་པ་དེའི་ལེ་ཚན་ཐ་མའི་ཤོག་གྲངས་ལས་ཚོད་དཔག་
བྱས་སོ།།
གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་ཞེས་བྱ་བའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་འདི་ལ་མཚན་
གཞན་ཤར་དྭ་ཏི་བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ཀྱང་བརྗོད་སྲོལ་ཡོད་འདུག ཟློས་གར་གྱི་གཞུང་འདི་ཉིད་
ཀྱི་ནང་ནང་གསེས་སྡེ་ཚན་ཁག་དགུ་ཡོད་ཅིང་། འདིའི་ནང་གཙོ་བོ་སྟོན་པས་ཤཱ་རིའི་བུ་
དང་མོང་གལ་བུ་གཉིས་སྟོན་པའི་བསྟན་པ་ལ་ཇི་ལྟར་ཞུགས་པའི་ཚུལ་གྱི་སྐོར་བསྟན།
དེའི་ནང་དེའི་སྐབས་ཀྱི་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་ཀྱི་གནས་སྟངས་དང་སྡེ་ཚན་སོ་སོའི་ནང་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་
དེའི་ནང་རྐུ་མ་དང་ཆང་རག སྨད་འཚོང་མ། ཁྲིམས་འགལ་བྱེད་མཁན་རྣམས་ཀྱི་ལོ་
རྒྱུས་ཉུང་ངུར་བསྡུས་ཏེ་བསྟན། ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་འདིའི་ནང་གི་འདྲེན་པ་ནི་
དྷིར་ཕྲཤཱནྟ་བྲམ་ཟེའི་རིགས་ཅན་ཞིག་ཡིན་ཅིང་འདྲེན་མ་ནི་སྨད་འཚོང་མ་འཆལ་སྤྱོད་ཀྱི་
བུད་མེད་གཅིག་ཡོད་པ་བསྟན། ཕྱིས་བུད་མེད་དེ་ཉིད་ཚུལ་མིན་གྱི་སྤྱོད་པ་དོར་ནས་རྒྱ་
གར་གྱི་ལུགས་སྲོལ་བཟང་པོའི་མཛངས་མའི་བུད་མེད་དུ་ཇི་ལྟར་འགྱུར་ཚུལ་བསྟན།

སློབ་དཔོན་རྟ་དབྱངས་ཀྱིས་མཛད་པའི་རྡོ་རྗེའི་ཁབ།
འདིའི་ནང་གཙོ་བོ་སྒེག་པའི་ཉམས་དང༌། བར་བར་ལ་བཞད་གད་དང་སྙིང་
རྗེའི་ཉམས་རྣམས་ཐབས་མཁས་པའི་ཚུལ་དུ་བསྟན་ཡོད་པ་བཤད། ཟློས་གར་གྱི་མཇུག་
བསྡོམས་སུ་སྟོན་པ་ཐུབ་པའི་དབང་པོ་དང་ཉན་ཐོས་ཆེན་པོ་ཤཱ་རིའི་བུ་བར་བགྲོ་གླེང་།
མཛད་བཞིན་པའི་ངང་རྫོགས་པར་བྱེད་དོ། བལྟ་བྱའི་སྙན་ངག་གི་ཟློས་གར་འདི་ཉིད་ལ་
གཞི་བྱས་ཏེ་ཕྱིས་སྙན་གྲགས་ཆེ་བའི་བློ་གར་གྱི་ཁྲབ་གཞུང་མཱལ་ཏེ་མཱདྷཝ་ལ་སོགས་
པའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་རྣམས་དེ་ཉིད་ལ་གཞིར་བྱས་པ་སེམས་སོ།།
བཞི་པ། གཟུགས་ཅན་ལྷག་མ་གཉིས་པ།?
འདི་ནི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་ཁྱད་པར་བ་ཞིག་ཡིན་ལ། གཟུ གས་སུ་
བཀོད་པའམ་དཔེ་ལ་སྦྱར་ཏེ་བཀོད་པའི་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་ཁྲབ་གཞུང་ཞིག་ཡིན་ཚོད་འདུག །
ཟློས་གར་འདིའི་ནང་འཁྲབ་བྱ་གཙོ་བོ་ནི་གྲགས་པ་དང༌། འཛིན་པ་དང༌། བློ་གྲོས་
གསུམ་གཙོ་ཆེར་བསྟན་ཅིང་། དེའི་སྔོན་དེ་ལྟ་བུའི་གཟུགས་བཀོད་ཀྱི་ཟློས་གར་མ་བྱུང་
བས་དེ་ཉིད་ཐོག་མ་ལྟ་བུ་ཡིན་ནོ། །དེ་ཉིད་ཡར་རྒྱས་སུ་ཕྱིན་ནས་ཕྱི་ལོ་བརྒྱ་ཕྲག་བཅུ་
པའི་རྗེས་སུ་པྲབོདྷ་ཙརྗོདཡ། སཾཀླཔ་སཱུ་པྱོདཡ་དང་ཨ་མྲྀ་ཏོདཡ་ལ་སོགས་པའི་གཟུགས་
ཅན་གྱི་སྙན་ངག་སྟེ་ཟློས་གར་བྱུང་བའོ།།

བུའི་རབ་བྱེད་ནང་གསལ་བའི་སྤྱོད་ཚུལ་ལྟ་བུ་ཡོད་ཅིང་། འདི་ཉིད་ཀྱི་ནང་འཁྲབ་སྟོན་པ་
གཙོ་བོ། རྒྱལ་སྲས་དྷན་ྗཡ་དང་ཤཱ་རིའི་བུ་དང་། མོད་གལ་ཡན་བུ་ཡིན་ལ། གྲོགས་ཀྱི་
ཚུལ་དུ་འཁྲབ་མཁན་གྱི་གྲས་སུ་གཡོག་མོ། མི་ངན། སྨད་འཚོང་མ་སོགས་ཡོད། ཟློས་
གར་གྱི་འཁྲབ་གཞུང་འདི་ཉིད་ཀྱང་ནཊྛཤཱསྡུ་ཟློས་གར་བསྟན་བཅོས་རྣམས་ཀྱི་དགོངས་
ཚུལ་ལྟར་རབ་བྱེད་དམ་ལེའུ་གཅིག་གིས་རྫོགས་པར་བྱེད་དོ།
གོང་བཀོད་ཟློས་གར་གྱི་བསྟན་བཅོས་འདི་རྣམས་གཙོ་བོ་ནང་པའི་ཆོས་ཀྱི་
ཁྱབ་སྤེལ་དང་། ནང་ཆོས་ཀྱི་ཁྱད་ཆོས་བསྟན་པ་མ་ཟད། དེའི་སྐབས་ཀྱི་སྤྱི་ཚོགས་ཀྱི་
གནས་སྟངས་དང་། ལེགས་བྱང་། ཆབ་སྲིད་སོགས་ཐུགས་སུ་བསྟན་པ་ལྟ་བུ་སྣང་ངོ༌། །
སློབ་དཔོན་གྱི་དེ་ལྟ་བུའི་གཞུང་མཛད་དགོས་དོན་གཙོ་བོ་ནི། སྟོན་པ་དང་དེའི་དམ་ཆོས་

Introduction
Ācārya Aśvaghosa's Vajrasūci is a unique thought and
history on social philosophy of ancient India and is a great
significance for the study of sociological studies that the historian
and sociologists have failed to give due importance which it
deserves. Before the advent of Buddha, ancient India reminisces of
sphere of social philosophy based on Varna division and the
justification of supremacy of Brāhmaṇas in the social grouping.
Buddha was the first to raise the issue of such a supremacy and
social injustice infested toward other three Varnas.' He taught
profusely on this subject and said that it was a myth created by
ignorance and guided by the principle of egoism by a handful of
people. The Buddha realized the seriousness of the problem of such
social inequality. This can be substantiated in the Brāhmana section
of Dhammapāda, Vāsettha sutta,2 Āsvalāyana sutta of
Majjimanikāya, Śārdūlakarņāvadāna of Divyāvadāna,3 Uddāna
varga etc. After that lines of his followers viz., Nāgārjuna,
Āryadeva4, Ācārya Candrakīrti, Ācārya Bhavaviveka, Ācārya
1
2
See, Dhammapada, Brāhmaṇa Vagga, p.536, Pāli and Tibetan Root-text
commented by Dr. Wangchuk Dorjee Negi, published by The Corporate
Body of the Buddha Educational Foundation, Taiwan, 2003.
See, 48 Vāsettha sutta Majjimanikaya, p. 983, published by Baudha Bharati,
1999.
See, 33 Śārdūlakarṇāvadāna, Divyāvadāna p. 314, edited by Dr. P. L. Vaidya,
published by the Mithila Institute, 1959.
See, Cittavisuddhi-prakarana, p. 8, edited by Prabhubhai Bhikhabhai Patel,

Ācārya Asvaghoșa's Vajrasūcī
Ašvaghosa and so forth raised the issue to the level of academic
level with honesty and reasoning.
Among the Buddhists savants Aśvaghoșa's criticism of
social superiority on the grounds of birth, he used the authentic
Brāhmanical texts to show their supremacy as sheer contradictory
what they are claiming. The Vajrasūci is outstanding on many
scores. He could not satisfy his convictions merely by presenting
remarks from the Buddhist point of view and reasoning. Thus, he
pierced like an adamantine needle as it were into the eyes of the
privilege orthodoxy to compel conscious of the gravity what they
professed are in loggerhead with their authentic texts. The text is to
be admired for its subtle debating skill that demolishes the thesis of
his opponents by quoting their own authentic scriptures. He never
once substantiated the utterances of the Buddha or any other
Buddhist authority in his support.
The text has a wider relevance even in today's society and
fabric social structure of the world at large. It is not confined to a
historical situation in Indian history and culture. It stares squarely
into the attitude, which may occur in any society and in any period
of time. Social discrimination on grounds of birth has been enforced
sometimes among the members of the same society. This often takes
a very ugly form as such an attitude arises on several grounds,
including economic disparity and political subjugations. The slaves
and helots in the ancient times and serfs in the feudal system has
driven humanity into a tortuous journey of long centuries, still such
pretentious prejudices and biases are faced today in many forms in
the so called twenty-first century where civilised society dream of a



Introduction
classless society over all development. In such a gloomy situation,
the theme presented in the Vajrasūcī will surely provide some
thought provoking, inspiring and heartening solace.
Analysis on Ašvaghoșa's biographical accounts based
on Indian and Tibetan literary sources:
The Indian literary sources are not in uniformity with birth
place of Aśvaghoșa, Some scholars opt for Kāśī, others state for
Pāțliputra the modern Patna and some opt for Sāketa (Ayodyā).
However, Sāketa seems to be correct as it is found mentioned in the
work of Aśvaghoșa's Saundarānanda Mahākāvyam. 'This is also
confirmed in the Aśvaghosa's drama called Sāriputra-prakarana2
edited and published by Prof. Luders.3
In Tārānātha's History of Buddhism Aśvaghoșa's birth
place was in the city of Khorta in Nalini in the east.4 Whereas Pawo

Analysis on Asvaghoșa various names occurring in
different Tibetan literature sources:
In Taranatha's History of Buddhism it runs thus, “Ācārya
Mātụceța a is the Brahamiņa called Durdharșakāla. His other epithets
are Śūra, Aśvaghoșa, Mātộceța, Pitsceța, Durdharsakāla,
Dharmasubhuti, Maticitra3.”
In the History of Buddhism in Tibet and Mongoliat it differs
slightly viz., “Other epithets of Ācārya Kāla or Śūravīra are Śūra,
Aśvaghoșa, Pitrceta, Mātrceta, Dharmasubhūti, Maticitra."
In the Chosjung Khespai Gaton gives reasons of various
epithets given to Asvaghoșa. It states that when the astrologer saw

Introduction
the palm of young , Aśvaghoşa adorned with sign of haritaki on his
palm. He proclaimed likewise,
“He who is charming and holds a medicinal vase,
Who possess fragrance and elegance,
Who sees with delightful eyes,
May he victorious who annihilates the sufferings”.
Thus he was given the name as Amrtaghata (he holds a nectar vase).
While he was born neighing like a horse he is called the Brāhamiņa,
Aśvaghoșa and whosoever sees this youth becomes joy therefore he
is called as Kumār Rāma. Later he was so respectful and devoted to
his parent's services he was renowned as Pitrceta and Mātrceta. He
learned medicine from Rși Dvipādācārya. Once a king's disease was
heeled by relocating the nerves of the toe and so forth he became
versatile in medicine. Thus it was acclaimed,
“The captain Sarvapāla is lord of the wealth,
The great victorious Pitrceţa is the lord of medicine,
Kaminga is the lord of war, and
The beautiful Prabhavati is the lord of gardens."
Thus, he is one of the four lords. He made penance for a
week and Siva manifested in front of him. He has given the name of
Durdhrsatakāla.
Apart from that Pawo Tsung-lag threngwa enumerates of
Ašvaghoșa as Maticitra, Asoka, Śrīmahaśubha, while he was a
Tairthika he was called as Jațādhari, Keſakambali and when he
became Buddhist he was known as Dharmasubhutighosa,

See, History of Buddhism entitled 'Scholar's Rejoicing' Vol. II, p. 1445,



72
Ācārya Aśvaghosa's Vajrasūcī
Dipamkara, Śūra, Lakșatikopadhyāya, Danstrasena,
Gandharvadhāra, Trideva and so forth.
Thus there are so many epithets occurs which has their own
source in Indian Buddhist literature which they have accredited.
Therefore, it is difficult to ascertain which are the real names of
Aśvaghosa or which are not.
The main crux of the problem in Tibetan literatures regarding
confusion of various epithets of Aśvaghosa lies in the recognising
three different Ācāryas viz., Aśvaghosa, Mātrceţa and Aryaśūra as
one.
Analysis of Asvaghoșa's parents name in the Tibetan
literature:
Ašvaghoṣa one of the leading scholarship in both Buddhist
and non-Buddhist learnings, the names of his parents do tend
different in various Buddhist Historical writings of the Tibetan
scholars. There is no uniformity found among the scholars' writings.
In Chosjung Khespai Gaton his father's name recorded as
Brāhmana physician Samgha Guhya and mother's name as Ratnā
Singh. However, in the commentary of Jatakamālas of Yongzin
Lobsang Tenzin his father's name was Brāhmiņa Simghaguhya and
mother's name Suvarņakṣī or Sukhavatī.1
However, both these distinct explanation can be traced to the
Indian origin. Aștanghrdyam of Vāgbhatta one of the three sages
(munitraya)—in analogy to the trinity of Sanskrit grammatical

many Tibetan History of Buddhism Ašvaghosa became a Buddhist
after he was defeated in a debate with Āryadeva, the direct disciple
of Ārya Nāgārjuna. Thus Ašvaghoṣa became disciple of Nāgārjuna
in his later part of his life. According to Buddhist tradition Arya
Nāgārjuna came 400 after the demise of the Buddha. Some western
scholars agree the advent of Nāgārjuna 100 B.C. which is close
enough with the date of the Buddhist tradition.
However, some Indian literary sources too differ the date of
Ašvaghosa nevertheless, many opt as the contemporary of Kaniska,
though there is no uniformity in Kaniska date too. Many scholars
opt his date 75 B.C. However, many scholars assert that Aśvaghoșa
is earlier than Nāgārjuna that contradicts the Tibetan literary sources.
This confusion may lie in accepting three or more Nāgārjunas by the
modern scholarship. It rather looks odd in accepting different
Nāgārjuna on the basis specialisation on particular scholarship viz.,
medicine, philosophy and tantra and so forth. However, in recent
years the literary findings of various texts relating to Nāgārjuna raise
eyebrows to the modern scholars stand of manifold Nāgārjuna.
While the late Prof. Jagannātha Upadhyāya took a journey as far in
1980 to Nepal for search of Buddhist Tantra manuscript. He came
across a tantric text composed by Nāgārjuna runs in the colophon as
Bhikṣu Nāgārjuna. Prof. Jagannātha Upadhyāya also confirmed that
the Sanskrit styles of both Mūlamadhyamika and the Tantra text
proves to be one author.1 In addition, the tradition too agree that

Biography of Ašvaghoșa preserved in the Tibetan
literary works:1
Once there lived a merchant in the city of Khorta in Nalini in
the east. He has ten daughters and were married them except the
youngest one. Later she was married to a rich Brāhmiņa called Singh
Guhya. A son was born and named as Krsna. He was taken to an
astrologer and he prophesied this boy to be an intelligent and hard
working, later he will become a great scholar. As per the Brāhmiņa
tradition he learnt the Sanskrit pros and con of its formulation as
well hymns to devas and devis. He further learnt the Vedas and its
branches and became erudite in all the learnings. He was particularly
was devoted to his parents, thus he was known as Pitrceta and
Matrceta. However, there are two versions why he named
Ašvaghoșa. Some assert that after his immediate birth the horses
strongly neighed, therefore he was given name. Others say that he
has a very beautiful voice while he preached teachings to the
populace even animals like horses listened carefully to his teaching
and at the same time neighed, thus he was given the name. The later

Translated by Lama Cimpa & Alaka Chattodyaya, edited by D. P.
Chattopadhyaya, Motilal Banarasidass, Delhi, 1970; See, History of
Buddhism entitled 'Sun Blossoming the Lotus' p. 49, by Kunkhyen Padma
Karpo, published by XXXI Kargyud Relief and Protection Committee,
Varanasi, India, 2004.

Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajrasūci

Dwivedi.1
Aśvaghoșa was also well versed in tirthika tantra and
ingenious logic. Therefore, he wished to be a Victor of all directions.
He went to a deep penance of Maheśvara for seven consecutive
days. To that Maheśvara was pleased and appeared before him ask
him what kind of boon he desires. He replied to be Victor of all
directions and Maheśvara bestowed the boon of formidable of
mankind. Maheśvara also gave a parrot well versed in all sciences, a
manifestation of Brahmā, a small slate, a manifestation of Visnu and
bhagini pandita, and a manifestation of umā as helper. If these three
are unable to defeat then Maheśvara himself will enter in him and
will become inevitable Victor of all the directions of mankind. so
saying he disappeared.
After that all Buddhist scholars were defeated in scholarly
debate and made them to follow tenet of the tirthika. All the viharas
were turned into Hindu temples. Those who do not adhere to the
tenet of the tirthika, their wealth were snatched and banished them.
In nutshell, the Buddhist doctrine was completely destroyed. Even
among tirthikas who do not take refuge to Maheśvara, for them,
hartedness was also inculcated. With pride of having a boon with a
wish to conquer, he marched to Oddivisa, Gauda, Tirhuta,
Kāmarupa and so forth places and defeated the Buddhists in debate
and put them into the Hindu fold. He made the Buddhists to make
1
See, Baudha Sanskrit Kāvya Saṁīkşa, pp. 135, Published by Banaras Hindu
University, Varanasi, 1976



Introduction
prostrate to the tirthika in order to insult them. Thus, he became
victorious to all directions and came to be known Durdhantakāla.
When he narrated to his mother about his victorious
campaign of defeating the Buddhists and the like, she was a devotee
of the Buddhist in disguise. So she thought that if she sends to
Nālandā University for debate then galaxy of scholars who are
versatile in all learnings would defeat him. Buddhists other places
are like the hair of a horse, but Buddhists of Magadha central India
are like hairs of a body of a horse. Unless you defeat them, your
victory over all direction is meaningless, thus she said to him. Then
he went to Nālandā University and declared for a debate and who
ever win the loser will accept the order of the winner. All the
scholars at Nālandā having heard his boon as well victorious
campaign they decided no other than Arya Nāgārjuna and his
disciple Aryadeva difficult to defeat Aśvaghosa. At that time Arya
Nāgārjuna and his disciple Aryadeva were residing at Śrīparvata in
south India. Therefore, all the Bhikṣus of Nālandā assembled and
conversed of sending invitation to teacher and his pupil. Finally they
wrote a letter and profuse supplication to the Mahākāla was made
and a crow from the heart of the stone statue of the Mahākāla took
the letter and flew to Śrīparvata to Ārya Nāgārjuna and his disciple
Āryadeva. Ārya Nāgārjuna said to Āryadeva that Aśwaghośa a
tirthika has made havoc at Nālandā and to ward off that I set forth.
To this Āryadeva replied it would be long journey so it is apt for
him to proceed. The teacher said that it is a great task of the doctrine
so he will set forth. With successive persuasion from Āryadeva,
they both agreed to debate taking position of a presentation and



78
Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajraşūcī
refutation of Buddhist and non-Buddhist standpoint. Āryadeva took
the stand point of Buddhist, whereas his teacher Nāgārjuna took
stand point of tirthika. At some point Āryadeva was so baffled that
his teacher was sticking to the tirthika's view point as a real tirthika
and he doubtful if his teacher a real Tirthika. To this stage his teacher
ask to stop the debate immediately. His teacher gave permission to
proceed to Nālandā but he said because doubted his teacher, so there
will come an obstacle on the way. The Nāgārjuna gave him some
substance of janghacarikā (miraculous power of swift-footedness).
On the way, Āryadeva met a tirthika woman who need an eye of a
learned bhikṣu to complete the materials required for her siddhi. On
being asked for it, he gave her one his eyes. He arrived at Nālandā in
a watch of the day.
At Nālandā Aśvaghoșa has declared that a huge debate
between him and any of Nāgārjuna and his disciples will take place
at Nālandā Āryadeva disguised as wood seller and his belongings
put inside, because no outsider was entertained to enter the
monastery. Aryadeva sent a message stating the he has come. The
monks of the Nālanda became very happy when the message was
received and invited him with great pomp and show.
At one time Āryadeva met at the pond Aśvaghoṣa offering
water to his ancestors. Āryadeva enquired what he was doing? He
replied he was offering water his dead ancestors. Āryadeva too
started offering to a clean place near it. He enquired what he was
doing? To this Āryadeva replied he was watering for a dry tree in
Śrīparvata in south India. To this he said what is the use of watering
here when the tree in south. To this Āryadeva replied how offering



Introduction
of water can benefit the deed ancestors who were born in other
births?
On another occasion Āryadeva met Aśvaghoṣa taking a dip
on the ghats of the Ganges. To this Āryadeva enquired what he was
doing? He replied he was cleansing his sins. Āryadeva then, started
cleaning a pot from outside filled with filth. He saw that and said
that how can that be clean when it is filled filth from inside with a
laughing stock. To this Aryadeva enquired when the mind afflicted
attachment, hatred and so forth defilements how can sins be purified
by cleaning the filthy body.
Aśvaghoșa as every day use count the monks presence since
he made the declaration for the debate, he found one more when
Aryadeva came to the monastery. To this elegantly enquired who is
the extra shaven head that he is not there before. To this Āryadeva
replied it came from the neck. Where does the neck came from he
counter enquired. Aryadeva replied it came from the head and he felt
now his debate counterpart has arrived.
Then Asvaghoșa went to the threshold of the door of the
monastery and said where I get in or not. To this Āryadeva replied it
depends to your desire. Then he took a parrot in hand said will it die
or not. Aryadeva replied that it depends to your compassion.
Thus, he thought he got the right counter part for the debate.
He invited the King with his ministers, nine galaxies of scholarship
of both sides as witness. Whosoever is defeated he will be send to
prison and cut his tongue and so forth rules were framed. On the
actual day of the debate Āryadeva collected a cat, mustard oil,
tattered cloth and a filthy old shoes as his resources and appliances.

Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajrasūci
Ašvaghosa too collected his resources and helper the learned parrot,
the slate television, Devi umā and Maheśvara and offered
supplication and bali. In front of all the learned witness including the
king and his ministers and sat facing each. In olden days before the
actual debate begins, in order to get into elaborate debate one begins
with joke. Aśvaghoșa seeing Aryadeva with only one eye he
sarcastically said how is it he has only one eye. Āryadeva replied
with following articulation in accord with prosody,
'Satakratu, Indra though having thousand eyes doe not see the
essence,
Rudra though having three eyes does not see the essence,
I, Āryadeva having only one eye, sees the essence of all the three
worlds'.
Then Aśvaghoșa said arrogantly you are not suitable opponent, first
you defeat my parrot, so saying he set forth the parrot, the
manifestation of Brahmā. Āryadeva then sent forth his cat and killed
the parrot. To that Aśvaghoșa said you contradicted the Buddhist
concept of non-violence. Āryadeva replied that this non-virtuous act
will be purified later to my teacher residing at Śrīparvata. To that
Aśvaghoșa enquired how could your teacher purify that non-
virtuous act of yours. Āryadeva counter attacked that how the non-
virtuous act of the cat killing your parrot come to me rather to the
cat. Then Aśvaghoșa said that you debate with my slate now. Then
Āryadeva hurled the jar of black oil on the slate and no more letters
were eligible. Then, Ašvaghoşa contemplated Umā and send bhagini
pandita to debate with Āryadeva. In return Aryadeva send a naked
youth in front of her and she was so shy she ran away. After that



Introduction
81
Aśvaghoṣa meditated Maheśvara but Aryadeva threw the filthy
clothe and Maheśvara could not enter into the body of Aśvaghoșa.
Thereafter, the final debate began with the presentation of the
tirthika view points viz., presentation of an omniscient and valid
Creator, a permanent sound that is the attribute of space, the
permanent self and a part less eternal theory of Primordial Principle
of Samkya were elaborated by Aśvaghoșa. Āryadeva refuted in
order with manifold presentation of reasoning and logical statements
refuting opponent's stand viz., Creator is not possible because a
permanent contradicts creating any thing and if such a Creator gives
boon and so forth then it would be absurdum as impermanence. The
permanent sound theory is also become redutio absurdum, because
sound is the result of palatal etc. place and effort of a person. A
permanent self also is not possible, because a self coming from one
birth and going to another is impermanent. Primordial of Principle
Samkya cannot be part less eternal because from it arises five
tanmatras, eleven senses and so forth. While Aryadeva presenting
the Buddhist view he made steadfast the concept of no action done
can not ripen, action done becomes inexhaustible, the intelligent of a
mental continuum of a person also increases through training and
exhaust the three poisons etc. are purified, finally one can attain
Arahathood. While one understands nature of two levels truth one
attains Buddha hood. Further, in this very life one can attain the
Buddha hood through tantra path thereby relying on a perfect
kalyanamitra, then receiving the initiations and empowerments and
gradual practice of the yugnadha and so forth were presented with
ingenious logics backed by scriptures. When both scholars



82
Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajrasūcī
presented their views all the scholars could understand them. When
both debaters engaged in the discussion on the profound subtleties,
then the learned witness spellbound. Thus, both the witnesses and
king were unable to decide who won or who lost.
When, Ašvaghoșa was unable to give reasonable answer, he
opted for display of miracles and he manifested himself into a
hundred eyed Indra. Then Āryadeva manifested into a thousand
eyed one and over shine him. Ašvaghosa then, set forth fire from his
mouth, to this Āryadeva poured water over it. Further, Aśvaghoșa
drew beautiful circles in the sky that was wiped away by winds send
forth by Aryadeva. Thus Aśvaghoșa, neither shine in his ingenious
logics nor in the miracles, he was extremely abashed. He thought he
was baffled and over came of his pride and arrogance. He thought to
fly to the Brahmā loka and flew in the sky Āryadeva too followed
him. When they reached in the acme of the sky Aryadeva said if you
precede this limit, then you will loose your life. If he does not
believe, then cut a log of his hair throw up, so saying he cut a log of
his hair it was cut into pieces, so he could not proceed ahead.
Conversion to Buddhism:
The Ārydeva took him on earth and hand over to the king.
Ašvaghoșa could not afford to cut his tuft and log of hair and tried
to jump into the Ganges. The king ordered his men to catch him and
he was put in a Buddhist vihara as house arrest. He sat in corner and
contemplated why he was defeated although he mastered all his
viewpoints of his tenets. So he was baffled and to thought to see the
Buddhist scriptures what worth is there. He read some texts, which
were extensive and profound in nature; especially he read



Introduction
Mañjuśrīmūlakalpatantral in which he found his prophesies of him
by Buddha. This moved him and a strong confidence inculcated in
him to the Buddha. He got fear of the undermining the theory of
causation (karma and phala) and underestimating Arydeva. He was
most remorseful for his actions done and he found the Buddha as
the only true teacher and refuge. Thus, he wrote2
'I prostrate to the principle Buddha,
I prostrate to the Dhamma, the refuge
I prostrate to the great Sangha
I always prostrate to the Triple Jewels.'
Then he went to Aryadeva, offered his bitter regret for his
wrong doings and put forth his wish to become ordained in his fold.
Āryadeva took him to Arya Nāgārjuna in Śrīparvata for ordination.
He duly listened to all tripitakas and four tantras and received all
instructions and became an eminent scholar of Buddhism. He came
to be known as the great Āryasūra, the holder of treasure of
instruction of the Acārya Nāgārjuna and his followers. Many of his
earlier followers of tirthikas too came into folder of Buddhism in
thousands. Tens and thousands of Brāhminas around Nālandā also
took refuge in the Buddhist fold. His embracing the Buddhism
spurred the alms and fortune of the viharas. There were two hundred

Once in his dream Ārya Tārā appeared and prophesied him
to compose more praises to the Buddha that will lessen his sins and
obscurations made toward Buddha-dharma. Through this extortion
antidote to whatever his underestimation created toward karma-phala
and so forth he composed sāmāya deśnā. Antidote for
underestimation to Buddha he composed Satapañcāśatka (one
hundred and fifty verses) praise to Buddha, Jātakamāla relating to
the ten perfections; varṇārhavarṇastotra etc., for dharma
underestimation he composed Dharmakāyastotra; for samgha he
composed gūrupañcaśati, mūlapattisaṁvara (root-downfall), for
karma-phala defamation he composed medical texts viz.,
astañgahrdayam, astañgasaṁgraha and aştañgavatāra.
In addition, he composed two well-known poetic
compositions one based on the life of Buddha called Buddhacarita
(Acts of the Buddha) and the on the life of his cousin Nanda called
Saundarānanda (The life story of Sundari and Nanda). His
compositions especially on the praises to Buddha became so well
known that disseminated to all parts and places. Even ordinary
bards, singers and jesters too sing in beautiful lines and pierced in
the mind of ordinary folks mind and made long felt faith toward
Buddha that enhanced the spread of Buddha-dharma for along time.
When he looked back to his earlier folder claim of what is
Brāhmaṇa and its philosophical view points were lacked substance
in contrast with what Brāhmana constituted in Uddāna and



Introduction
85
Dhammapada of Buddhist fold. He composed Vajrasūcī refutation
of four castes quoting profusely on the basis of earlier writings of
Smſtis, Mahābhārata etc. He has also composed a drama called
Sariputra-prakarana, based on the life of Sāriputra one of the two
main disciples of Buddha, through which the common people
develop deep and steadfast faith and confidence in Buddha. There
were two texts called Mahāyānaśraddhotpāda, a treatise (Developing
faith in Mahāyāna) and Sūtrālamkāra (Ornament of the Sūtra),
which were not translated into Tibetan but were translated into
Chinese language. His many other compositions relating to
philosophy etc. are given in the end of the introduction.
In his later life he was invited by king Kaniska, however, he
sent his emissary in his place, as he was quite old at time. He also
sent a letter to the king, which is preserved in Tibetan translation in
the letter section of Tangyur. He sent his disciple Jñānakīrti as his
tutor. Finally, he contemplated the various difficult to perform acts
of Buddha and moved by the compassionate ones motivation he, too
went into the near forest and found a hungry tigress with her young
ones and pricked his blood veins and nourished young ones and in
the end contemplating the Buddha's compassionate act, he wrote the
saptatipranidhana by his blood and gave his body to the tigress and
her young ones. Thus, came the end of this great teacher and in true
footprints of the Tathāgata as prophesized in the Mañjuśrīmūlakalpa-
tantra as referred as the non-returning Bodhisattva.
Analysis to the biography,
According to Indian scholars the above biography has been
incorperated all the biographies of three acāryas three into one viz.,



86
Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajrasūcī
Aśvaghosa , Matrceța and Sūra are put into one. However, all the
Indian scholars the assert that three ācārya are all contemporaries of
king Kaniska. Further, many opt that litrary styles are similar too.
Especially, some view that the saptati-pranidhana is not by
Matrceťa but of Parahitaghosanatha whose date is later. Some
scholars are view Ašvaghosa was born in Saketa but lived a long
time in Kasmīr and Gandhara. However, some opt that when
Aśvaghosa was residing in Peśāvar he came into huge debate with
Buddhist Bhikṣu called Pārśva in front huge gatherings of scholars,
Ašvaghosa was defeated Buddhist Bhiksu Pārsva initiated him into
Buddhist fold. Bhikṣu Pārśva was a well-known and established
scholar in ingenious logics and a master of Buddhist and non-
Buddhist learnings. Whereas, some scholars assert that Bikksu
Punyayasa initiated him into Buddhist fold. Some claim that when
king Kaniska invaded and conquered Magadha in central India with
his army, he was betaken by the scholarly learnings of Aśvaghoșa
and he took with him to Peśāvar. Ašvaghosa was already initiated
into Buddhist fold and he established himself an eminent scholar.
However, some scholars are in the view that Kaniska and his army
attacked Magadha from west and eventually conquered Patliputra,
the capital. The king was defeated and initiated into Buddhist fold.
Then he met Asvaghoṣa became delighted to his erudition as a
Buddhist scholar and took along with him to Peśavar. When the
ācārya arrived in Peśāvar he came into contact with manifold
cultures viz., Turk, Greek, Śāka, Persian and so forth and found
many similarities of Indian culture in them. The king offered the
ācārya the post king's poet of the court for his wide and well versed
in all the learnings. The Chinese history too refers similar
biographical account of the ācārya. It is also mentioned that the



Introduction
ācārya was the purohita of the king while Caraka was his physician.
Some Japanese scholars Ācārya Nāgārjuna came after
Ašvaghoșa. They claim that Ācārya Nāgārjuna wrote a commentary
on Mahāyāna Sraddhotpāda composed by Aśvaghoșa.
Analysis of Asvaghoșa's tenet-
There is no uniformity among scholars to which four
Buddhist tenets Ašvaghosa professed. In accordance to the Tibetan
accounts he got initiated according to the vinaya tradition of
Mulasarvāstivāda, however, asserted Madhyamika philosophy. This
does not contradict his date, as this time the Mahāyāna was in full
swing and during the time of Kaniska the various divisions of
scholars claim that Asvaghoșa, Āryaśūra and Matrceta all were great
poets but they are all different persons. The reason behind is there is
difference in the style of composition; there is difference of their
dates and there is difference of their birthplace and name of their
parents. However, the Tibetan accounts they all are one single
person.
Ašvaghoșa's works not translated into Tibetan:

Vajrasūcī
Vajrasūcī's Theme:
The Vajrasūcī, deliberately examines the quest what is
Brāhmaṇa? Is the soul Brāhmana? Is a man by birth Brāhmaṇa or he
is a Brāhmaṇa by his knowledge? Is he Brāhmaṇa by his actions, or
by his profession or by his mastery over the Vedas? Aśvaghosa
quotes from the Vedas, Mahābhārata and Manusmrti, where it is
shown that soul is not Brāhmaṇa, as the same should becomes birds,
beasts, human beings as well gods in different births. He quotes
from Smrtis to prove that one does not become Brāhmaṇa by birth
or case. He profusely quotes great sages like Viśvamitra, Kapila and
so many others become Brāhmaṇas, though they were not born from
Brāhmana mothers. If someone objects the mother is not a
Brāhmana, but the father is Brāhmana. The author substantiates that
1
See, Saundarānanda Mahākāvyam, recently translated into Tibetan by Ladakhi
scholar Ācārya Lobsang Jamspal and published by the Institute under the
Bibliotheca Indo-Tibetica Series-xliv, 1999



Introduction
those who are born from maidservants, conceived by Brāhmaṇas,
will also be entitled to be Brāhmaṇas. However, Brāhmaṇas do not
want this! Moreover, whether the Brāhmanas of the modern times
are born from Brāhmana fathers is very doubtful. Because it is seen
in ancient times that the wives of the Brāhmaṇas had illicit
connections with other men of all castes, even with Sudra. Thus,
Brāhmaṇa by birth is absurd.
The body too can not be Brāhmaṇa if it is Brāhmaṇa, then in
the funeral ceremony when the son lits the pyre of his father, then he
commits Brahamanicide i.e. sin of killing a Brāhmana. Further, if the
body is Brāhmaṇa, then all the four castes become Brāhmaṇa as they
were born from the body of the Brahmaā Does one become
Brāhmana by knowledge? Certainly not. Then all who have
knowledge would become Brāhmaṇa. There are many Sudras who
are well versed in the Vedas, and all branches of knowledge.
However, they do not become Brāhmaṇa. One is not Brāhmana by
his actions or profession either. There are many persons in other
castes who follow the profession of a Brāhmana, but they are not
called a Brāhmana. Then who is the Brāhmana? What Brāhmana-
hood means? Brāhmana-hood means abstinence from all sins. It is
clean and beautiful like the Kunda flower and the Moon.Truth is
Brāhmana-hood, austerity is Brāhmana-hood, control over the
senses is Brāhmaṇa-hood, compassion towards all sentient beings is
the characteristic of a Brāhmaṇa. He further justifies the position that
humanity is one family, because there is differences or distinction of
any kind found in the body of the Brāhmaṇa and other castes, as we
find among different animals or among different trees. Neither do



Ācārya Asvaghoșa's Vajrasūci
we find any difference in feelings: in happiness, in suffering, in fear
or pain. Thus, by caste we all are one and not different.
In concluding he says: 'In order to destroy the delusion of
the Brāhmaṇas who have lost all their reasons, what we have said
here, let the honest person accept if it is reasonable, otherwise reject
them.'
Authorship of Vajrasūcī:
The entire available various Manuscript attribute the work to
Aśvaghoșa. However, the Chinese translation attributes it to
Bodhisattva Dharmakīrti, which was made by Dharmadeva between
973 and 981 A.D. But this translation seems to be so obscure and
defective that it could not be made out whether is really a translation
of the original work or a commentary. There existed omissions and
in many places even alterations of the original. Thus, it appears to be
a different text, a similar work of the same nature probably an
adaptation of the original Vajrasūci by Dharmakūti, Eminent scholar
Prof. Sylvian Levi too suggests it an adaptation of an earlier treatise
composed originally by Aśvaghosa.1 Therefore there is no definite
evidence against Aśvaghosa being the author of the Sanskrit text of
Chinese translation.
The Vajrasūcī became first known to the English-knowing
scholars when B. H Hodgson and L. Wilkinson translated into
English in 1829 and Published it in the Transactions of the Royal
Asiatic Society, Vol. III, 1835 tiled as A Disputation respecting
Caste by Aśvaghoșa. Both translators were charmed by democratic
1
Journal Asiatique, 1908, S. 10, T. XII, p. 71.



Introduction
spirit of the author this ancient text, who defends the equality of all
classes of human beings: "as they are equal in feelings—in joy and
sorrow, in life, in intellect, in conduct, in birth and death, in sexual
enjoyment, in fear."
In addition, there are internal evidences to prove the antiquity
of the work. Throughout the work, old texts are referred to: Vedas,
the Mahābhārata and the Mānavadharma. Nowhere there is any
mention of the Purāņas. The author says in his introductory verse:
“The Vedas and Smrtis are the authorities.”
Prof. Sujitkumar Mukhopadhyāya too expresses this view:
"From all these it appears, at that time, when the work was
composed, the Purānas either not composed at all or were not old, or
well known enough to be quoted in the work of distinguished
author.”
Otherwise, the author who seems to be well versed in the
Brāhmaṇical traditions must have quoted various useful to the
content and more suitable passages than what has been quoted.
Some scholars like Winternitz raises eyebrow against the
authorship of Ašvaghoșa are:
a) It is not enumerated either by I-tsing or in the Tibetan
Tangyur among the works of Ašvaghosa
b) In the Catalogue of Chinese Tripitaka, a translation of
Vajrasūci which said to contain "a refutation of the four Vedas,"
which was made by Dharmadeva between 973 and 981 A.D. is
accredited to Dharmakīrti,.1
1
See, A History of Indian Literature, Vol. II, 266.



92
Ācārya Aśvaghoşa's Vajrasūcī
However, the above objections are not serious one, for
a) There are some important works of Aśvaghoșa which are
neither enumerated by I-tsing nor found in the Chinese and Tibetan
Tripitaka. For instance, the Saundarnānadamahākavyam and the
Sāriputra Prakarana are not enumerated by I-tsing nor found in the
Chinese and Tibetan Tripitaka.
b) As already substantiated above the Chinese version which
is attributed to Dharmakīrti appears to be a different work, a similar
work of the same nature fundamentally different from the original
Vajrasūcī. In the original there is nowhere any refutation of
Brāhmiņical scriptures. On the contrary, it is the Brahminical
scriptures are used as its support. While in the Chinese Vajrasūcī,
there is refutation of the four Vedas, which are foundation of
Brāhminical scriptures.
Asvaghoşa's Vajrasūcī in various translations:
1) This text was first translated into Chinese in the tenth century
(973-981) by Dharmadeva;
2) In 1859 the German scholar Prof. A. Weber translated this text
into German and published in ABA Journal, May 1859;
3) The Japanese translation was made by Dr. J. Takasuku;
4) The first English translation of this text was made by B. H.
Hudson and published by L. Willkinson, R. A. S. Vol. 3, 1829.
5) Prof. Mukhopadyāya made English translation in 1950 and
published in the Sino-Indian Cultural Society, śānti Niketan,

Higher Studies, Sarnath, Varanasi, 2006.
Mahāyāna Śraddhotpāda Šāstra:
This is a treatise of Mahāyāna, which elucidates the
principles of the philosophical viewpoints. The original of Sanskrit
Manuscript is lost, however, there existed two Chinese translations.
The first one is of Paramārtha (also known as Kulanātha), which
was translated into Chinese in circa 557 A.D. with aid of interpreters
and scholars of Lian or Liang Dynasty. This is found in the collected
works of Paramārtha. The second is by Śikṣānanda (695-700) A.D.,
an Indian Buddhist living in that country. He said to have brought
Sanskrit original text and also found the older Sanskrit Mss. in the
T'ezuan tower. Later Vantsag, an eminent Korean translator also
translated that became famous in China as well in Japan. It became
so popular that it has as many 170 commentaries written on it by
various scholars.1 This is kept in the syllabus of the many
universities of Japan.
1
See, The Awakening of Faith, intro. p. 5, note 4, translated with commentary
by Yoshito S. Hakeda, Colombia University Press, New York, 1966.



Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajrasūci
On Paramārtha Chinese translation three different English
translations were published in 1900 A.D. by Prof. Teitaro Suzuki,
the second is of Timothy Richard published in 1907 A.D. and third
by Chinese monk Vai-Tao in 1937 A.D. In 1967 Prof. Yoshita S.
Hakeda published another English translation of this Vajrasuci with
commentary, which is far the best one among all the available
English translations. 1
The subject matter is divided into five parts viz., proving
Mahāyāna as the word or teaching of the Buddha; refutation of
expressing that the presentation of two truths as not being teaching
of the Buddha; proving it as the teaching of the Buddha; this text is
being explained in five techniques of expositions viz., purpose,
summary, word by word explanation, conjunction and presentation
of opponents query and answer.
Sūtrālamkāra:
This text is a compendium of all Jātakas of Budhha's former
lives. This text is a beautifully woven into both versifications as well
in prose form poetry. The Sanskrit original text is not available,
however, Kumārjīva translated this text into Chinese in 405 i.e. fifth
century. French scholar Huber translated this text into French and
published in 1907 A.D. The main purpose for composing this text
was to prove Mahāyāna as the teaching of the Buddha; how a
devotee of the Buddha who have taken refuge in him should follow
into the foot-steps of Buddha's previous lives acts as a Bodhisattva;
1
See, The Awakening of Faith, translated with commentary by Yoshito S.
Hakeda, Colombia University Press, New York, 1966.



Introduction
95
how even for a single being's happiness the Bodhisattva gave his
life as well his belongings; to prove that there existed life before or
after death and inculcate undaunting steadfast faith in the Buddha
and so forth.
There is no doubt that this text is the composition of
Ašvaghoșa. It also highlights that his text is earlier than
Buddhacarita, as there are many verses quoted from this text. In this
text also enlightens the situation of social fabric of his time, culture,
various religious folds prevalent at that time, it also elucidates the
presence of two epics viz., Rāmayāna and Mahābhārata highly
known in the society. He also quotes from these two epics in this
text. Apart from that in this text he presents the position of tirthika
viewpoint in general and particularly Jaina, Nyāyika and Vaiseșika
philosophies and then refutes them one by one. This text important
text needs to be translated into Tibetan and hope in future aspirant
may take this pious project and see its completion.
Saundarānanda Mahākāvyām:
This poetic text was not found in the Tibetan translation.
However, in recent year Ladakhi scholar Lobsang Jampal with great
effort and hard work the Tibetan translation was conceived and
published by the Central Institute of Higher Studies. It contains
eighteen chapters in total. This is a well known in India, the second
best composition by Aśvaghoṣa in the field of poetry. Some
scholars are in the view that this text is a supplementary of
1
See, Published by the Central Institute of Higher Tibetan Studies under the
Bibliotheca Indo-Tibetica Series-xliv, 1999



96
Ācārya Asvaghoşa's Vajrasūci
Buddhacarita, as in this text Buddha's biographical note is more
elaborate than one finds in the Buddhacarita. The text depicts with
utmost flavour and stylish Sanskrit phrases, which is lucid, and easy
grasping one beautifully knitted with peaceful emotion; showing the
worldly life of Buddha's cousin Nanda and his wife Sundarī. In
addition, Buddha's valuable teachings intertwined into elegance and
flavour of Sanskrit poetic compositions are articulated. As a
consequence, pain of separation from his newly wed wife got
solaced and eventually became one his disciples who later attained
Arhathood, the cessation of suffering. This epic has all the quality as
characteristics of a māhakavyam. Nanda is the actor and Sundarī as
his actress mainly intertwined with peace emotion but other
emotions are articulated as and when needed in this epic. The main
theme is the Buddha's ethical teaching based on love and
compassion with the view of interdependent origination, spurring
for end of suffering not only for Nanda but for larger section of
livings that are attracted to worldly pleasures due to distorted view
and there by following the wrong way. The epic is written for larger
welfare and benefit of the sentient being. This epic also give
encouragement to the mankind to understand ones responsibility and
ward off from the lust and so forth negativities which is harmful to
oneself as well to others. Many a scenes from Saundarānanda have
been popular with sculptors, but palace-life of Nanda and Sundari
seems to have been very popular with contemporary and post-
Aśvaghosa artists.
In Mathura museum and Gandhara art also depicts Nanda
arranging the hair of Sundarī, who is looking into a mirror, while



Introduction
female attendant is holding a toilet basket. Gandhara Art now in
National Museum, Delhi displays Sundarī's toilet and Nanda's
conversion.2 R. Side—Nanda is making the hair of Sundarī. L.
Side—Nanda is standing besides Buddha, with a bowl in his hands,
in a worshipping pose, yet reluctant to accept conversion. "This is a
remarkably well-carved panel, illustrating the touching story of the
newly wedded Nanda and his beautiful wife Sundarī, whom he had
abandoned, to become a monk".3 Thus, this epic found most
probably popular among the common masses and his gīti-kāvya of
this epic were sung by the bards and jesters of those days which the
sculptors depicted which are more lively and touching to the
common people's heart and spreading the Buddha's import in all the
walks of the people.
The author on one hand find full success in giving right path
to their dumb— suffering and on the other hand, he is not less
successful in depicting the valuable teachings of Buddha with so
skillfully in its style of elegance and flavour.
Drama:
Aśvaghoṣa is not only known for his gifted in gīti-kāvya and
epic writer but a great dramatist too. He was most gifted one this
field especially to depict Buddha's message to the general public
who are not well-versed in the literary filed. Among the reputed
dramas he composed the following five dramas are most important
ones viz., i) Rāstrapāla drama, Urvaſīviyoga drama, First remaining

metaphor of Sāriputra-prakarana, Second remaining metaphor of

a) Rāstrapāla drama:
Among the five minor science the drama is also of the
sciences. At present only the name of this drama is mentioned by the
great Indologist Rahul Samkrtyāyana and also by the eminent
scholar Prof. Sylvain Levi. However, Ācārya Baladevo Upadhyāya
in his 'A history of Sanskrit Literature' writes that the Rāstrapāla
drama composed by Aśvaghosa is given in Vādirājsuri's Jain
Nyāyaviniscayavivarna.1 The author has written a scholarly
commentary as well as shown Asvaghoșa as the author of the
Rāstrapāla drama. This also confirms that Aśvaghoșa was a great
writer on drama and during his time drama was staged among the
common people as also sung by the bards.
There is a story occurring in Majjhima Nikāya called
Ratthapāla Sutta, which might be the basis of this drama. The actor
of this drama called Rāstrapāla, a councilor born in the country of
Kurus in market town called Thhullakotthita. Being the only child of
his parents, he sought the permission to enter the fold of Buddha
and got with much difficulty. Soon by his super knowledge and
diligent study and practice he attained the Arhathood. Then, one day

with permission of the Buddha, he went to see his parents with a
begging bowl in his hands. He was provided with a stale food at his
father's house, which he took happily. The next day he was allured
with wealth and his wife so that he returned home. But it had no
effect because he was fully awakened one. He replied "These are
Sir, four expandings of dhamma expounded by the Buddha who
knows, who sees, perfected one, because I have known and seen
and heard these, I have gone forth from home into homeless". The
four truths are: the unstable world is brought to end, the world is
refuge, no protection, the world is not ones own, one must leave it
leaving everything...and the world lacks inherent existence is
unsatisfied, a slave to craving". These words was impressed the
king Koravya and he accepted the Buddha's fold.
There is also a Mahāyāna sūtra, called Rāstrapālapariprccha,
in which Buddha gave answers to the queries of Rāstrapāla about
the practices, leading to the attainment of Bodhi, the Buddhahood. 1
Urvašīviyoga drama:
This is one of the drama first written by Aśvaghoșa and the
Urvaśī is the main character of the drama. This drama is perhaps
written before he came into fold of Buddha. Rahulsamkſtyāyana
writes in Volga to Ganga2 that before Aśvaghosa took refuge in the
Buddhist fold, his relationship with a beautiful and charming Greek
girl Prabhā was the subject of those days, but could not materialised

Ācārya Aśvaghoșa's Vajrasūcī
into marriage, due to difference in caste bindings. Thus, this drama
was the offshoot of his separation from Prabhā he might have
written such a drama, depicting the actual life story conceiving into
Urvašīviyoga drama, which was very famous and widely staged
drama of those days. It seems that it was first time Sanskrit drama
staged in Saketa and from there spread to far off places.
Rahulsamkrtyāyana opts that this was the first Sanskrit drama ever
staged. However, the original Sanskrit text is not available.
I Śāriputra-prakaraña drama:
Prof. Luders found the Manuscript of Sāriputra-prakarana,
three fragments form from Turfan in Central Asia, which was
written on palm leaves. The first metaphor Sāriputra-prakarana
depicts the life story of Śāriputra, one of the main disciples of
Buddha. This drama is also known by 'Sāradvatīputra-prakaraṇa'
another name of Sāriputra. On the basis of the first and last
colophon description the author as well number of text could be
visualised. The story also depicts both of Buddha's main disciples
viz., Śāriputra and Maudgalyāyana came into the fold of Buddha.
The story goes that both Sāriputra and Maudgalyāyana were born in
Brāhmiņa family and both were very fast friends. Once they said to
each other whosoever finds meaningful pursuit, then both of them
will share. Once Śāriputra came across with Aśvajita whose face
was radiant and calm going to door with a begging bowl in his hand.
He enquired who his teacher was.



Introduction
101
He replied1
'All phenomena are due to cause
The cause has been taught by the Tathāgata
The cause has also cessation
Thus, spoke my great teacher (Mahāśramana)'.
Śariputra was so impressed by this Buddha's teaching through this
verse. This verse elucidates the crux of Buddhist philosophy of
twelve links of Interdependent Origination. With thorough analysis
of this verse, he cultivated a deep faith in the Buddha, perceived the
way how phenomena really existed and became an Arhat
simultaneously. He later he repeated this verse to his close friend
Maudgalyāyana thrice, and he too became an Arhat and saw the true
nature of all phenomena.
In addition, the drama depicts all walks of life in those days
viz., thieves, pickpockets, drunkards, prostitutes and so forth. This
can be included as Hetaera Drama too where bad characters of the
society are prominently depicted. In accord to the rules of
Dramaturgy, the actor of this drama is a steadfast and calm Brahmin
whereas the actress is a prostitute by profession but depicted as an
ideal India woman. In this drama the emotion is predominantly
peaceful, passion, comedy and compassion given with elegance
style. The drama comes to end with a dialogue between Buddha and
Sāriputra. The metaphor applied in this drama can be seen in the later
Mrcchkațika drama. After that this style is followed in Mālatā-
Mādhava and so forth dramas in later period.

See, Mahāvagga, Vinayapitaka, p. 60 Baudha Bharati, 1998.

II Śāriputra-prakaraņa drama:
This fragment of the drama is special kind of metaphoric
one. This can be termed as Allegorical play. The characters involves
in this drama are viz., Fame, Steadfast and Wisdom and so forth.
There is account of such metaphoric drama so far. Thus, it can be
termed as the first Allegorical play in Sanskrit. One sees the
maturation and development of this style in Prabodhcandrodaya,
Samkalpa-suryodaya, Amrtodaya and so forth in ten century A.D.
III Śāriputra-prakaraṇa drama:
This fragmented drama is also the work of Aśvaghoșa. In
this drama also similar to ſāriputra-prakarana has been depicted the
characters. The main characters are Dhananjaya, a prince, Sāriputra
and Maudgalyayāna. In the lesser characters maidservant, wicked
and prostitute etc. are depicted. The story has very similar character
of poor Cārudutta and Mșcchkațika. This drama too is written in
accord to the rules of dramaturgy and play.
The composition of above dramas were made to disseminate
and spread the message of Buddha's benevolent acts to the common
masses through visual poetic compositions which is more powerful
and heart touching. However, the importance of moral ethics, the
importance of political, social, cultural and philosophical aspect is no
less in these dramas. By judging with these peculiarities it is clear
that the main objective of Aśvaghoşa's excellent literary works is to
focus Buddha, his benevolent teachings to all walks of life and its
philosophical implications, nevertheless, other characteristics such as
socio-economic etc. are also taken up to the larger audience.

मूलग्रन्थ
གཞུང་དངོས།



वज्रसूची
ओं नमो मञ्जुनाथाय।
जगद्गुरुं मञ्जुघोषं नत्वा वाकायचेतसा ।
अश्वघोषो वज्रसूची सूत्रयामि यथामतम् ॥१॥
वेदाः प्रमाणं स्मृतयः प्रमाणं धर्मार्थयुक्तं वचनं प्रमाणम् ।
यस्य प्रमाणं न भवेत्प्रमाणं कस्तस्य कुर्याद्वचनं प्रमाणम् ।।२।।
(क) इह भवता यदिष्टं 'सर्ववर्णप्रधानं ब्राह्मणवर्ण' इति, वयमत्र
ब्रूमः, कोऽयं ब्राह्मणो नाम। किं जीवः किं जातिः किं शरीरं किं ज्ञानं
किमाचारः कि कर्म किं वेद इति ।
(ख) तत्र जीवस्तावद् ३ ब्राह्मणो न भवति। कस्माद् । वेदस्य
प्रामाण्याद् । उक्तं हि वेदे-
(ग) 'ओं सूर्यः पशुरासीत्५, सोमः पशुरासीद्, इन्द्रः पशुरासीत् ।'
पशवो देवाः। आद्यन्ते देवपशवः। श्वपाका अपि देवा भवन्ति।
(घ) अतो वेदप्रामाण्यान्मन्यामहे जीवत्वाद् ब्राह्मणो न भवति।
भारतप्रामाण्यादपि।
उक्तं हि भारते:
सप्तव्याधा दशार्णेषु मृगाः कालञ्जरे गिरौ ।
चक्रवाकाः शरद्वीपे हंसाः सरसि मानसे ॥३॥
तेऽपि जाताः कुरुक्षेत्रे ब्राह्मणा वेदपारगा:११ ।।४।।
(ङ) अतो भारतप्रामाण्याद् व्याधमृगहंसचक्रवाकदर्शनसम्भ-
वान्मन्यामहे १२ जीवस्तावद् ब्राह्मणो न भवति। मानवधर्मप्रामाण्यादपि।



108
आचार्याश्वघोषकृत वज्रसूची
उक्तं हि मानवे धर्मे१३–
अधीत्य चतुरो वेदान्साङ्गोपाङ्गेन तत्त्वतः ।
शूद्रात्प्रतिग्रहग्राही ब्राह्मणो जायते खरः ॥५॥
खरो द्वादशजन्मानि षष्टिजन्मानि शूकरः१४ । ।
श्वानः सप्ततिजन्मानि-इत्येवं मनुरब्रवीत् ॥६॥
(च) अतो मानवधर्मप्रामाण्याज्जीवस्तावद् ब्राह्मणो न भवति।
(छ) जातिरपि ब्राह्मणो न भवति। कस्मात्? स्मृतिप्रामाण्याद् ।
उक्तं हि स्मृतौ-
हस्तिन्यामचलो जात उलूक्यां केशपिङ्गलः ।
अगस्त्योऽगस्तिपुष्पाच्च कौशिकः कुशसम्भवः१५ ॥७॥
कपिलः कपिलाजातः शरगुल्माच्च१६ गौतमः ।
द्रोणाचार्यस्तु कलशात्तित्तिरिस्तित्तिरीसुतः ।।८।।
रेणुकाऽजनयद्राममृष्यशृङ्गमुनिं मृगी८ ।
कैवर्तिन्यजनयद् व्यासं कुशिकं चैव शूद्रिका ॥९॥
विश्वामित्रं च चण्डाली२२ वसिष्ठं३ चैव उर्वशी ।
न तेषां ब्राह्मणी माता लोकाचाराच्च ब्राह्मणाः ॥१०॥
(ज) अतः स्मृतिप्रामाण्यान्मन्यामहे २४ जातिस्तावद् ब्राह्मणो न
भवति।
(झ) अथ मन्यसे माता वाऽब्राह्मणी भवेत् । तेषां पिता ब्राह्मणस्ततो
ब्राह्मणो भवतीति। यद्येवं दासीपुत्रा अपि ब्राह्मणजनिता ब्राह्मणा भवेयुः।
न चैतद्भवतामिष्टम्।



वज्रसूची
109
(ब) किं च। यदि ब्राह्मणपुत्रो ब्राह्मणस्तर्हि ब्राह्मणाभावः प्राप्नोति।
इदानीन्तनेषु ब्राह्मणेषु पितरि सन्देहाद्। गोत्रब्राह्मणमारभ्य ब्राह्मणीनां
२५शूद्राभिगमनदर्शनाद् । अतो२६ जातिर्ब्राह्मणो न भवति ।२७ मानवधर्म-
प्रामाण्यादपि।
उक्तं हि मानवे२८ धर्मे २९–
सद्यः पतति मांसेन लाक्षया लवणेन च ।
त्र्यहाच्छूद्रश्च भवति ब्राह्मणः क्षीरविक्रयी ॥११॥
आकाशगामिनो विप्राः पतन्ति मांसभक्षणात् ।
विप्राणां पतनं दृष्ट्वा ततो मांसानि वर्जयेत् ॥१२॥
(ट) अतो मानवधर्मप्रामाण्याज्जातिस्तावद् ब्राह्मणो न भवति। यदि
हि जातिर्ब्राह्मणः स्यात्, तदा पतने३१ शूद्रभावो नोपपद्यते। किं खलु
दुष्टोऽप्यश्व:३२ सूकरो३३ भवेत्? तस्माज्जातिरपि ब्राह्मणो न भवति ।
(ठ) शरीरमपि ब्राह्मणो न भवति ।३५ कस्माद्३६? यदि शरीरं
ब्राह्मणः स्यात् तर्हि पावकोऽपि ब्रह्महा ३७ स्याद् । ब्रह्महत्या च बन्धूनां
शरीरदहनाद्भवेद्। ब्राह्मणशरीरनिष्यन्दजाताश्च क्षत्रियवैश्यशूद्रा अपि
ब्राह्मणाः स्युः। न चैतद् दृष्टं । ब्राह्मणशरीरविनाशाच्च यजनयाजना-
ध्ययनाध्यापनदानप्रतिग्रहादीनां ब्राह्मणशरीरजनितानां फलस्य विनाशः
स्यात्। न चैतदिष्टम्३८ । अतो मन्यामहे शरीरमपि ब्राह्मणो न भवति ।३९
(ड) ज्ञानमपि ब्राह्मणो न भवति। कुतः? ज्ञानबाहुल्याद्। ये ये
ज्ञानवन्तः शूद्रास्ते सर्व एव ब्राह्मणाः स्युः। दृश्यन्ते४० च क्वचित् शूद्रा
अपि वेदव्याकरणमीमांसासांख्यवैशेषिकनग्नाजीवकादिसर्वशास्त्रार्थ-
विदः। न च ते ब्राह्मणाः स्युः। अतो मन्यामहे ज्ञानमपि ब्राह्मणो न
भवति।
(ढ) आचारोऽपि ब्राह्मणो न भवति। कुतः? यद्याचारो ब्राह्मणः
स्यात्४१ तदा ये य आचारवन्तः शूद्रास्ते सर्वे ब्राह्मणाः स्युः। दृश्यन्ते च



110
आचार्याश्वघोषकृत वज्रसूची
नटभटकैवर्तभण्डप्रभृतयः४२ प्रचण्डतरविविधाचारवन्तो न च ते ब्राह्मणा
भवन्ति। तस्मादाचारोऽपि ब्राह्मणो४३ न भवति।
(ण) कर्मापि ब्राह्मणो न भवति। कुतः? दृश्यन्ते हि क्षत्रिय-
वैश्यशूद्रा यजनयाजनाध्ययनाध्यापनदानप्रतिग्रहप्रसङ्गविविधानि कर्माणि
कुर्वन्तो, न च ते ब्राह्मणा भवतां सम्मताः। तस्मात्कर्मापि ब्राह्मणो न
भवति।
(त) वेदेनापि ब्राह्मणो न भवति। कस्माद्? रावणो नाम
राक्षसोऽभूत्। तेनाधीताश्चत्वारो वेदाः। ऋग्वेदो यजुर्वेदः सामवेदोऽथर्व-
वेदश्चेति। राक्षसानामपि गृहे गृहे वेदव्यवहारः प्रवर्तत एव। न च ते
ब्राह्मणाः स्युः। अतो मन्यामहे वेदेनापि ब्राह्मणो न भवतीति ।४५
(थ) कथं तर्हि ब्राह्मणत्वं भवति।
उच्यते-
ब्राह्मणत्वं न शास्त्रेण न संस्कारैर्न जातिभिः ।
न कुलेन न वेदेन न कर्मणा भवेत्ततः४७ ॥१३॥
(द) कुन्देन्दुधवलं हि ब्राह्मणत्वं८ नाम सर्वपापस्यापाकरण-
मिति ४९ १५०
(ध) उक्तं हि-व्रततपोनियमोपवासदानदमशमसंयमो५१पचाराच्च ।५२
तथा चोक्तं वेदे५३–
निर्ममो५४ निरहङ्कारो निःसङ्गो निष्परिग्रहः ।
रागद्वेषविनिर्मुक्तस्तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः ।।१४।।५
सर्वशास्त्रेऽप्युक्तम्५६-
सत्यं ब्रह्म तपो ब्रह्म ब्रह्म चेन्द्रियनिग्रहः ।
सर्वभूते दया ब्रह्म एतद् ब्राह्मणलक्षणम् ।।१५॥



वज्रसूची
111
सत्यं नास्ति तपो नास्ति नास्ति चेन्द्रियनिग्रहः ।
सर्वभूते दया नास्ति एतच्चाण्डाललक्षणम् ॥१६॥
देवमानुष"नारीणां तिर्यग्योनिगतेष्वपि ।
मैथुनं नाधिगच्छन्ति ते विप्रास्ते च ब्राह्मणाः ॥१७॥
शुक्रेणाप्युक्तम्६० :
न जातिर्दृश्यते तावद् गुणाः कल्याणकारकाः ।
चण्डालोऽपि हि तत्रस्थस्तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः ॥१८॥
(न) तस्मान्न जातिर्न जीवो न शरीरं न ज्ञानं नाचारो न कर्म न वेदो
ब्राह्मण इति।
(प) अन्यच्च भवतोक्तम्-'इह शूद्राणां प्रव्रज्या न विधीयते।
ब्राह्मणशुश्रूषैव तेषां धर्मो विधीयते। चतुर्पु वर्णेष्वन्ते वचनात्ते नीचा'
इति।
(फ) यद्येवमिन्द्रोऽपि नीचः स्यात्। 'श्वयुवमघोनामतद्धिते ६१' इति
सूत्रवचनात् । श्वा इति कुक्कुरः । युवा इति पुरुषः। मघवा इति सुरेन्द्रः।
तयोः श्वपुरुषयोरिन्द्र एव नीचः स्यात्। न चैतद् दृष्टं६२ किं हि वचनमात्रेण
दोषो भवति । तथा च। उमामहेश्वरौ। दन्तौष्ठमित्यपि लोके प्रयुज्यते । न च
दन्ताः प्रागुत्पन्ना उमा६३ वा। केवलं वर्णसमासमात्रं क्रियते
ब्रह्मक्षत्रविटशूद्रा६४ इति। तस्माद्या भवदीय५-प्रतिज्ञा 'ब्राह्मणशुश्रूषैव तेषां
धर्मः' [सा] न भवति।
(ब) किं चानिश्चितोऽयं ब्राह्मणप्रसङ्गः।
उक्तं हि मानवे६६ धर्मे६७-
वृषलीफेनपीतस्य निःश्वासोपहतस्य च ।
तत्रैव च प्रसूतस्य निष्कृतिर्नोपलभ्यते ॥१९॥



112
आचार्याश्वघोषकृत वज्रसूची
शूद्रीहस्तेन यो भुंक्ते मासमेकं निरन्तरम् ।
जीवमानो भवेच्छूद्रो मृतः श्वानश्च जायते५८ ।।२०।।
शूद्रीपरिवृतो विप्रः शूद्री च गृहमेधिनी ।
वर्जितः पितृदेवेन रौरवं सोऽधिगच्छति९ ।।२१।।
(भ) अतोऽस्य वचनस्य प्रामाण्यादनियतोऽयं ब्राह्मणप्रसङ्गः ।
(म) किं चान्यत्। शूद्रोऽपि ब्राह्मणो भवति। को हेतुः? इह हि
मानवे धर्मेऽभिहितम्-
अरणी गर्भसम्भूतः कठो७३ नाम महामुनिः ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातस्तस्माज्जातिरकारणम् ॥२२॥
कैवर्तीगर्भसम्भूतो व्यासो ४ नाम महामुनिः५ ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातस्तस्माजातिरकारणम्६ ।।२३।।
उर्वशीगर्भसम्भूतो वसिष्ठोऽपि महामुनिः ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातस्तस्माज्जातिरकारणम् ।। २४।।
हरिणीगर्भसम्भूत ऋष्यशृङ्गो महामुनिः ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातस्तस्माजातिरकारणम् ।।२५।।
चण्डालीगर्भसम्भूतो विश्वामित्रो महामुनिः ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातस्तस्माज्जातिरकारणम् ।।२६।।
ताण्डुली गर्भसम्भूतो नारदो हि महामुनिः ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातस्तस्माज्जातिरकारणम् १ ॥२७॥
जितात्मा निष्प्रतिद्वन्द्वः पञ्च जित्वा यतेन्द्रियः ।
तपसा ब्राह्मणो जातो २ ब्रह्मचर्येण ब्राह्मण:८३ ।। २८ ।।
न च ते ब्राह्मणीपुत्रास्ते च लोकस्य ब्राह्मणाः ।
शीलशौचमयं ब्रह्म तस्मात्कुलम"कारणम् ।।२९॥



वज्रसूची
113
शीलं प्रधानं न कुलं प्रधानं
कुलेन किं शीलविवर्जितेन ।
बहवो नरा नीचकुलप्रसूताः
स्वर्ग८७ गताः शीलमुपेत्य धीराः ॥३०॥
(य) के पुनस्ते कठव्यासवसिष्ठऋष्यशृङ्गविश्वामित्रप्रभृतयो११
ब्रह्मर्षयो नीचकुल २प्रसूतास्ते च लोकस्य ब्राह्मणाः। तस्मादस्य
वचनस्य९३ - प्रामाण्यादप्यनियतोऽयं ब्राह्मणप्रसङ्ग इति, शूद्रकुलेऽपि
ब्राह्मणो भवति।
(र) किं चाप्यन्यद् भवदीय मतम्-
मुखतो ब्राह्मणो जातो बाहुभ्यां क्षत्रियस्तथा९६ ।
ऊरुभ्यां वैश्यः संजातः पद्भ्यां शूद्रक एव च ।।३१।।
(ल) अत्रोच्यते। ब्राह्मणा बहवो न ज्ञायन्ते कुतो मुखतो जाता
ब्राह्मणा इति। इह हि कैवर्तरजकचण्डालकुलेष्वपि ब्राह्मणाः सन्ति ।
तेषामपि चूडाकरणमुञ्जदण्ड ९काष्ठादिभि:०० संस्काराः क्रियन्ते । तेषामपि
ब्राह्मणसंज्ञा क्रियते। तस्माद् ब्राह्मणवत्क्षत्रिया१०१दयोऽपि। इति पश्याम
एकवर्णः, नास्ति चातुर्वर्ण्यमिति ।
(व) अपि च। एकपुरुषोत्पन्नानां कथं चातुर्वर्ण्यम् । इह कश्चिद्देवदत्त
एकस्यां स्त्रियां चतुरः पुत्राजनयति। न च तेषां वर्णभेदोऽस्ति। अयं
ब्राह्मणोऽयं क्षत्रियोऽयं वैश्योऽयं शूद्र इति। कस्मात्? एकपितृकत्वाद् ।
एवं ब्राह्मणादीनां कथं चातुर्वर्ण्यम् ।१०२
(श) इह हि १०३ गोहस्त्यश्वमृगसिंहव्याघ्रादीनां पदविशेषो दृष्टः।
गोपदमिदं हस्तिपदमिदमश्वपदमिदं मृगपदमिदं सिंहपदमिदं व्याघ्रपद-
मिदमिति। न च ब्राह्मणादीनां१०४ ब्राह्मणपदमिदं क्षत्रियपदमिदं वैश्य-
पदमिदं शूद्रपदमिदमिति। अतः पदविशेषाभावादपि पश्याम एकवर्ण :,
नास्ति चातुर्वर्ण्यम्।

आचार्याश्वघोषकृत वज्रसूची
(ष) इह गोमहिषाश्वकुञ्जरखरवानरछागैडकादीनां भगलिङ्ग-
अतोऽप्यविशेषादेक एव वर्ण इति।
(स) अपि च। यथा हंसपारावतशुककोकिलशिखण्डिप्रभृतीनां रूप-
वर्णलोमतुण्डविशेषो दृष्टः, न तथा ब्राह्मणादीनाम्। अतोप्यविशेषदेक एव
वर्ण इति।
__(ह) यथा वटबकुलपलाशाशोकतमालनागकेशर०५शिरीषचम्पक-
प्रभृतीनां वृक्षाणां विशेषो दृश्यते, यदुत१०६ दण्डतश्च पत्रतश्च पुष्पतश्च
फलतश्च त्वगस्थिबीजरसगन्धतश्च, न तथा ब्राह्मण१० क्षत्रियविट्शूद्रा-
णामङ्गप्रत्यङ्गविशेषो न च त्वङ्मांसशोणितास्थिशुक्रमलवर्णसंस्थान-
विशेषणं नापि प्रसवविशेषो दृश्यते१०८ । ततोऽप्यविशेषादेक एव वर्णो
भवति।
(क्ष) अपि भो ब्राह्मण सुखदुःखजीवितबुद्धिव्यापारव्यवहार-
मरणोत्पत्तिभयमैथुनोपचारसमतया नास्त्येव विशेषो ब्राह्मणादीनाम्।
(त्र) इदं चावगम्यताम्। यथैकवृक्षोत्पन्नानां फलानां नास्ति वर्णभेद
उदुम्बरपणसफलवद्। उदुम्बरस्य हि पणसस्य च फलानि कानिचित्
शाखातो भवन्ति कानिचिद् दण्डतः कानिचित्स्कन्धतः कानिचिन्मूलतः।
न च तेषां भेदोऽस्तीदं ब्राह्मण१०९फलमिदं क्षत्रियफलमिदं वैश्यफलमिदं
शूद्रफलमिति। एकवृक्षोत्पन्नत्वाद्। एवं नराणामपि नास्ति भेदः।
एकपुरुषोत्पन्नत्वाद् ।११०
___ (ज्ञ) अन्यच्च दूषणं भवति। यदि मुखतो१११ जातो भवति ब्राह्मणो
ब्राह्मण्याः कुत उत्पत्तिः। मुखादेवेति चेद्? हन्त तर्हि भवतां भगिनी-
प्रसङ्गः स्यात्। तथा गम्यागम्यं न सम्भाव्यते। तच्च लोकेऽत्यन्तविरुद्धम्।
तस्मादनियतं ब्राह्मण्यम् ।११२
(अ) क्रियाविशेषेण खलु चतुर्वर्णव्यवस्था क्रियते। तथा च
युधिष्ठिराध्येषितेन वैशम्पायनेनाभिहितं क्रियाविशेषतश्चातुर्वर्ण्यमिति :

पाण्डोस्तु'१३ विश्रुतः पुत्रः स वै नाम्ना युधिष्ठिरः ।
वैशम्पायनमागम्य प्राञ्जलिः परिपृच्छति ॥ ३२।।
के च१४ ते ब्राह्मणाः प्रोक्ताः किं वा ब्राह्मणलक्षणम्।
एतदिच्छामि भो ज्ञातुं तद्भवान् व्याकरोतु मे ॥३३॥
वैशम्पायन उवाच :
क्षान्त्यादिभिर्गुणैर्युक्तस्त्यक्तदण्डो निरामिषः ।
न हन्ति सर्वभूतानि प्रथमं ब्रह्मलक्षणम्११५ ॥३४॥
यदा सर्वं परद्रव्यं पथि वा यदि वा गृहे ।
अदत्तं नैव गृह्णाति द्वितीयं ब्रह्मलक्षणम्१६ ।। ३५।।
त्यक्त्वा क्रूरस्व१७भावं तु निर्ममो निष्परिग्रहः ।
मुक्तश्चरति यो नित्यं तृतीयं ब्रह्मलक्षणम्१८ ॥३६॥
देवमानुष १९नारीणां तिर्यग्योनिगतेष्वपि ।
मैथुनं हि सदा त्यक्तं चतुर्थं ब्रह्मलक्षणम् ॥३७।।
सत्यं शौचं दया शौचं शौचमिन्द्रियनिग्रहः ।
सर्वभूतदया शौचं तपः शौचञ्च२१ पञ्चमम्१२२ ॥३८॥
पञ्चलक्षणसम्पन्न ईदृशो यो भवेद् द्विजः ।
तमहं ब्राह्मणं ब्रूयां शेषाः शूद्रा युधिष्ठिर ॥३९॥
न कुलेन न जात्या वा क्रियाभिर्ब्राह्मणो भवेत्१२३ ।
चण्डालो२४ऽपि हि वृत्तस्थो ब्राह्मणः स युधिष्ठिर २५ ।।१०।१२६
किं च भूयो वैशम्पायनेनोक्तम् :
एकवर्णमिदं पूर्वं विश्वमासीद् युधिष्ठिर ।
कर्मक्रियाविशेषेण चातुर्वर्ण्य प्रतिष्ठितम्१२७ ॥४१।।



116
आचार्याश्वघोषकृत वज्रसूची
सर्वे वै योनिजा माः सर्वे मूत्रपुरीषिणः ।
एकेन्द्रियेन्द्रियार्थाश्च तस्माच्छीलगुणैर्द्विजाः ।। ४२।।
शूद्रोऽपि शीलसम्पन्नो गुणवान् ब्राह्मणो भवेत् ।
ब्राह्मणोऽपि क्रियाहीनः शूद्रात्प्रत्यवरो१२८ भवेत्१२९ ।। ४३।।
इदं च वैशम्पायनवाक्यम् :
पञ्चेन्द्रियार्णवं घोरं यदि शूद्रोऽपि तीर्णवान् ।
तस्मै दानं प्रदातव्यमप्रमेयं युधिष्ठिर । ४४।।
न जातिर्दृश्यते राजन् गुणाः कल्याणकारकाः ।
जीवितं यस्य धर्मार्थे १३० परार्थे यस्य जीवितम् ।
अहोरात्रं चरेत्क्षान्तिं तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः१३१ ।। ४५।।
परित्यज्य गृहावासं ये स्थिता मोक्षकाक्षिणः ।
कामेष्वसक्ताः कौन्तेय ब्राह्मणास्ते युधिष्ठिर ३२ ।।४६।।
अहिंसा निर्ममत्वं चा३२मतकृत्यस्य वर्जनम् ।
रागद्वेषनिवृत्तिश्च एतद् ब्राह्मणलक्षणम् ।। ४७।।
क्षमा दया दमो दानं सत्यं शौचं स्मृतिघृणा ।
विद्या विज्ञानमास्तिक्यमेतद् ब्राह्मणलक्षणम्१३५ ।। ४८।।
गायत्रीमात्र ३६सारोऽपि वरं३७ विप्रः सुयन्त्रितः ।
नायन्त्रितश्चतुर्वेदी१३८ सर्वाशी सर्वविक्रयी'३९ ।। ४९।।
एकरात्रोषितस्यापि या गतिर्ब्रह्मचारिणः ।
न तत्क्रतुसहस्त्रेण प्राप्नुवन्ति युधिष्ठिर ४० ।।५०॥
पारगं सर्ववेदानां सर्वतीर्थाभिषेचनम् ।
मुक्त१४१श्चरति यो धर्मं तमेव ब्राह्मणं विदुः १४२ ।।५१।।

१३. मनुस्मृतिः, १०,१०६-११० भाव-साम्य के लिये तुलनीय।

ग्रामे गृहे वा ये द्रव्यं पारक्यं विजने स्थितम् ।
नाभिनन्दति वै नित्यं.. ........................।।
-महाभारत, अनुशासन-पर्व, १४४.३२
११७. -स्य-, बंगाल-हस्तलेख।
११८. क्रोधः शत्रुः शरीरस्थो मनुष्याणां द्विजोत्तम ।
यः क्रोधमोहौ त्यजति तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः ।।
यो वेदेदिह सत्यानि गुरुं संतोषयेत च ।
हिंसितश्च न हिंसेत तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः ।।
जितेन्द्रियो धर्मपरः स्वाध्यायनिरतः शुचिः ।
कामक्रोधो वशे यस्य तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः ।।
यस्य चात्मसमो लोको धर्मज्ञस्य मनस्विनः ।
सर्वधर्मेषु चरतस्तं देवा ब्राह्मणं विदुः ।।
धर्म तु ब्राह्मणस्याहुः स्वाध्यायं दममाजवम् ।
इन्द्रियाणां निग्रहं च शाश्वतं द्विजसत्तम ।।-महाभारत, वन-पर्व, २०६.३२-९
शौचेन सततं युक्तः सदाचारसमन्वितः ।
सानुक्रोशश्च भूतेषु तद् द्विजातिषु लक्षणम् ।। -महाभारत, शान्ति-पर्व, १८९.१८
११९. मनुष्य, बंगाल-हस्तलेख।
१२०. -ते-, मद्रास-हस्तलेख।
१२१. -न्तु, बंगाल-हस्तलेख।
१२२. तीर्थशौचमनर्थित्वमार्जवं सत्यमार्दवम् ।
अहिंसा सर्वभूतानामानृशंस्यं दमः शमः ।।
-महाभारत, अनुशासन-पर्व, १०८.४
अद्भिर्गात्राणि शुध्यन्ति मनः सत्येन शुध्यति ।
विद्यातपोभ्यां भूतात्मा बुद्धिानेन शुध्यति ।।
क्षान्त्या शुध्यन्ति विद्वांसो दानेनाकार्यकारिणः ।
प्रच्छन्नपापा जप्येन तपसा वेदवित्तमः ।। -मनुस्मृति, ५.१०६-९

.१४
सत्यं तीर्थ क्षमा तीर्थ तीर्थमिन्द्रियनिग्रहः ।
सर्वभूतदयातीर्थं सन्तोषस्तीर्थमेव च ।।
ब्रह्मचर्य परं तीर्थ नियमस्तीर्थमुच्यते ।
ज्ञाननं तीर्थ धृतिस्तीर्थमहिंसा तीर्थमुच्यते ।।
-पद्म-पुराण, २.२३७; १२-१५ (आनन्दाश्रम, पूना, संस्करण)
१२३. न च, बंगाल-हस्तलेख।
१२४. चण्डालौ, पूना-हस्तलेख।
१२५. न कुलेन न जात्या वा क्रियाभिर्ब्राह्मणो भवेत् ।
चण्डालोऽपि हि वृत्तस्थो ब्राह्मणो यक्षपुङ्गव ।।
शृणु यक्ष कुलं तात न स्वाध्यायो न च श्रुतम् ।
कारणं हि द्विजत्वे तु वृत्तमेव न संशयः ।।
-महाभारत, वन-पर्व, ३१३.१०८
न जटाहि न गोत्तेन न जच्चा होति ब्राह्मणो ।
यम्हि सच्चं च धम्मो च सो सुची सो च ब्राह्मणो ।।
-धम्मपद, ब्राह्मणवग्गो २६, श्लोक ११
१२६. अहिंसा ब्रह्मचर्यं च विशुद्धाच्च प्रतिग्रहः ।
फलेन न समर्थं च ब्राह्मणः स्याधुधिष्ठर ॥
यह श्लोक बंगाल तथा इण्डिया आफिस, लन्दन हस्तलेख के कोष्ठक में ही उपलब्ध है ।
१२७. किं ब्राह्मणा ये सुकृतं त्यजन्ति किं क्षत्रिया लोकमपालयन्तः ।
स्वधर्महीना हि तथैव वैश्याः शूद्राः स्वमुख्यक्रियया विहीनाः ।।
तस्मान्न गोऽश्ववत्कश्चिज्जातिभेदोऽस्ति देहिनाम् ।
कार्यशक्तिनिमित्तस्तु संकेतः कृत्रिमो भवेत् ।।
-भविष्य, ब्राह्मण, ४०.३३-३४
